# Ottoman Empire - Wikipedia

\["

[![\"Page](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/Semi-protection-shackle.svg/20px-Semi-protection-shackle.svg.png/%22)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wikipedia:Protection_policy#semi\%22 "\\"Cet")

","

[![\"Écoutez](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Sound-icon.svg/20px-Sound-icon.svg.png/%22)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/File:Wikipedia_-_Ottoman_Empire_-_Main_History.ogg/%22 "\\"Écoutez")

","

Turkish empire (ca. 1299–1922)

\\n

Cet article concerne l'empire. Pour le califat associé, voir [Califat ottoman](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate/%22 "\\"Califat") .

\\n

\\n

L' **Empire ottoman** <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-35\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">[</font></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> l </font></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">]</font></font></span></a></sup> ( [/ ˈ ɒ t ə m ə n /](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Help:IPA/English/%22 "\\"Aide : API/anglais\\"") <sup class="\&quot;ext-phonos-attribution" noexcerpt="" navigation-not-searchable\"=""><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/File:LL-Q1860_(eng)-Flame,_not_lame-ottoman.wav/%22" title="\&quot;Fichier:LL-Q1860" (eng)-flamme,="" pas="" boiteux-ottoman.wav\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">ⓘ</font></font></a></sup> ), également appelé l'**Empire turc**, <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-36\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> [</font></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> 24</font></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> ] </font></font></span></a></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-37\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-37\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">[</font></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> 25</font></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> ]</font></font></span></a></sup> était un[royaume impérial](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Empire/%22 "\\"Empire\\"") <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-38\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> [</font></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> m</font></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> ]</font></font></span></a></sup> qui contrôlait une grande partie de[l'Europe du Sud-Est](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Southeast_Europe/%22 "\\"Europe"),[de l'Asie occidentale](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/West_Asia/%22 "\\"Asie")et[de l'Afrique du Nord](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/North_Africa/%22 "\\"Afrique")du 14e au début du 20e siècle ; il contrôlait également des parties du sud-est[de l'Europe centrale](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Central_Europe/%22 "\\"Europe"), entre le début du 16e et le début du 18e siècle. <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-39\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-39\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> [</font></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> 26</font></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> ] </font></font></span></a></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-40\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">[</font></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> 27</font></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> ] </font></font></span></a></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-41\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">[</font></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> 28</font></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> ]</font></font></span></a></sup> \\n

L'empire est né d'un [*beylik*](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anatolian_beyliks/%22 "\\"Beyliks") , ou [principauté](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Principality/%22 "\\"Principauté\\"") , fondé dans le nord-ouest  de [l'Anatolie](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anatolia/%22 "\\"Anatolie\\"") vers 1299 par le chef tribal [turkmène](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkoman_\(ethnonym\)/%22 "\\"Turkoman") [Osman Ier](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Osman_I/%22 "\\"Osman") . Ses successeurs [conquirent](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe/%22 "\\"Ottoman") une grande partie de l'Anatolie et s'étendirent aux [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Balkans/%22 "\\"Balkans\\"") au milieu du XIVe siècle, transformant leur [petit royaume](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Petty_kingdom/%22 "\\"Petty") en un empire transcontinental. Les Ottomans mirent fin à l' [Empire byzantin](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Byzantine_Empire/%22 "\\"Byzantine") avec la [conquête de Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople/%22 "\\"Fall") en 1453 par [Mehmed II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_II/%22 "\\"Mehmed") . Avec sa capitale à [Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Istanbul#Ottoman_Empire\%22 "\\"History") (aujourd'hui [Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Istanbul/%22 "\\"Istanbul\\"") ) et contrôlant une partie importante du [bassin méditerranéen](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin/%22 "\\"Mediterranean") , l'Empire ottoman fut au cœur des interactions entre le [Moyen-Orient](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Middle_East/%22 "\\"Middle") et l'Europe pendant six siècles. Régnant sur de nombreux peuples, l'empire accorda divers niveaux d'autonomie à ses nombreuses communautés confessionnelles, ou *[millets](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\)/%22 "\\"Millet")* , pour gérer leurs propres affaires conformément à [la loi islamique](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Islamic_law/%22 "\\"Islamic") . Sous les règnes de [Sélim Ier](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Selim_I/%22 "\\"Selim") et [de Soliman le Magnifique](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent/%22 "\\"Suleiman") , l'Empire ottoman devint une [puissance mondiale](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Global_power/%22 "\\"Global") . <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-42\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">[</font></span></a></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-42\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> 29 </font></a></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-42\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">]</font></span></a></sup>/%22 "\\"Turkmène")*/%22 "\\"Millet")*<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-42\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""></font></span></a></sup>\\n

Alors que l'on pensait autrefois que l'Empire ottoman était entré dans une [période de déclin](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Decline_Thesis/%22 "\\"Thèse") après la mort de Soliman le Magnifique, le consensus académique moderne postule que l'empire a continué à maintenir une économie, une société et une armée flexibles et fortes pendant une grande partie du XVIIIe siècle. Les Ottomans ont subi des défaites militaires à la fin du XVIIIe et au début du XIXe siècle, culminant avec la [perte de territoires](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Decline_and_modernization_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Déclin") . Avec [la montée du nationalisme](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"La") , un certain nombre de nouveaux États ont émergé dans les Balkans. Suite aux réformes *[Tanzimat](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tanzimat/%22 "\\"Tanzimat\\"")* au cours du XIXe siècle, l'État ottoman est devenu plus puissant et organisé en interne. Lors de la [révolution de 1876](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/1876_Ottoman_Revolution/%22 "\\"Révolution") , l'Empire ottoman a tenté [une monarchie constitutionnelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era/%22 "\\"Première") , avant de revenir à une dictature royaliste sous [Abdul Hamid II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II/%22 "\\"Abdul") , après la [Grande Crise d'Orient](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Great_Eastern_Crisis/%22 "\\"Grande") . \\n

À la fin du XIXe siècle, les intellectuels ottomans, connus sous le nom de [Jeunes-Turcs,](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Young_Turks/%22 "\\"Jeunes") cherchèrent à libéraliser et à rationaliser la société et la politique selon les principes occidentaux, ce qui aboutit à la [Révolution des Jeunes-Turcs](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution/%22 "\\"Révolution") de 1908, menée par le [Comité Union et Progrès](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress/%22 "\\"Comité") (CUP), qui rétablit [une monarchie constitutionnelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era/%22 "\\"Deuxième") . Cependant, après les désastreuses [guerres balkaniques](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Balkan_Wars/%22 "\\"Guerres") , le CUP se radicalisa et se nationalisa de plus en plus, [menant un coup d'État en 1913](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat/%22 "\\"Coup") qui instaura une dictature. \\n

Français Aux XIXe et début du XXe siècles, [la persécution des musulmans pendant la contraction ottomane](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_during_the_Ottoman_contraction/%22 "\\"Persécution") et [dans l'Empire russe](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#Russian_Empire\%22 "\\"Persécution") a entraîné des pertes en vies humaines à grande échelle et [une migration massive vers la Turquie actuelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muhacir/%22 "\\"Muhacir\\"") en provenance des [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Balkans/%22 "\\"Balkans\\"") , [du Caucase](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caucasus/%22 "\\"Caucase\\"") et [de Crimée](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crimean_Khanate/%22 "\\"Khanat") . <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-43\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-43\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">[</font></font></span><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""> 30 </font></font><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;"><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"=""><font style="\&quot;vertical-align:" inherit;\"="">]</font></font></span></a></sup> Le CUP a rejoint [la Première Guerre mondiale](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/World_War_I/%22 "\\"Première") aux côtés des [puissances centrales](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Central_Powers/%22 "\\"puissances") . Il a lutté contre la dissidence interne, en particulier la [révolte arabe](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Arab_Revolt/%22 "\\"Révolte") , et s'est engagé dans [un génocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Late_Ottoman_genocides/%22 "\\"Génocides") contre [les Arméniens](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_genocide/%22 "\\"génocide") , [les Assyriens](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Assyrian_genocide/%22 "\\"génocide") et [les Grecs](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Greek_genocide/%22 "\\"génocide") . Au [lendemain de la Première Guerre mondiale , les](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I/%22 "\\"Les") [puissances alliées](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I/%22 "\\"Alliés") victorieuses ont occupé et [partagé](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Partage") l'Empire ottoman, qui a perdu ses territoires du sud au profit du [Royaume-Uni et de la France . La](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement/%22 "\\"Accord") [guerre d'indépendance turque](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence/%22 "\\"Guerre") victorieuse , menée par [Mustafa Kemal Atatürk](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk/%22 "\\"Mustafa") contre les Alliés occupants, a conduit à l'émergence de la [République de Turquie](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkey/%22 "\\"Turquie\\"") et à l' [abolition de la monarchie ottomane](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Ottoman_sultanate/%22 "\\"Abolition") en 1922.\\n

\\n\\n

## Étymologie

\\n

See also: [Osman I § Name](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Osman_I#Name\%22 "\\"Osman")

\\n

The word *Ottoman* is a historical [anglicisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anglicisation_\(linguistics\)/%22 "\\"Anglicisation") of the name of [Osman I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Osman_I/%22 "\\"Osman"), the founder of the Empire and of the ruling [House of Osman](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty/%22 "\\"dynastie") (also known as the Ottoman dynasty). Osman's name in turn was the Turkish form of the Arabic name *[ʿUthmān](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Uthman_\(name\)/%22 "\\"Othman")* (عثمان). In [Ottoman Turkish](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish/%22 "\\"turc"), the empire was referred to as *Devlet-i ʿAlīye-yi ʿOsmānīye* (دولت عليه عثمانیه), lit. '**Sublime Ottoman State**', or simply *Devlet-i ʿOsmānīye* (دولت عثمانيه‎), lit. '**Ottoman State**'.\\n

The Turkish word for \\"Ottoman\\" (*Osmanlı*) originally referred to the tribal followers of Osman in the fourteenth century. The word subsequently came to be used to refer to the empire's military-administrative elite. In contrast, the term \\"Turk\\" (*Türk*) was used to refer to the Anatolian peasant and tribal population and was seen as a disparaging term when applied to urban, educated individuals.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-44\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-44\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>31<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 26\"="">: 26 </span></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-45\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>32<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In the [early modern period](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Early_modern_period/%22 "\\"Période"), an educated, urban-dwelling Turkish speaker who was not a member of the military-administrative class typically referred to themselves neither as an *Osmanlı* nor as a *Türk*, but rather as a *Rūmī* (رومى), or \\"Roman\\", meaning an inhabitant of the territory of the former [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Byzantine_Empire/%22 "\\"Empire") in the Balkans and Anatolia. The term *Rūmī* was also used to refer to Turkish speakers by the other Muslim peoples of the empire and beyond.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-46\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>33<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 11\"="">: 11 </span></sup> \\n

In Western Europe, the names Ottoman Empire, Turkish Empire and Turkey were often used interchangeably, with Turkey being increasingly favoured both in formal and informal situations. This dichotomy was officially ended in 1920–1923, when the newly established [Ankara](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ankara/%22 "\\"Ankara\\"")\-based [Turkish government](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Grande") chose Turkey as the sole official name. At present, most scholarly historians avoid the terms \\"Turkey\\", \\"Turks\\", and \\"Turkish\\" when referring to the Ottomans, due to the empire's multinational character.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Soucek-2015_47-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Soucek-2015-47\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>34<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

## History

\\n

Main article: [History of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Histoire")

\\n

See also: [Territorial evolution of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Évolution")

\\n

### Rise (c. 1299–1453)

\\n

Main article: [Rise of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rise_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"L'essor")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Sultan_Uthman_I.jpg/250px-Sultan_Uthman_I.jpg/%22)

[Ottoman miniature](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_miniature/%22 "\\"Miniature") of [Osman I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Osman_I/%22 "\\"Osman") by Yahya Bustanzâde (18th century)

\\n

As the [Rum Sultanate](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum/%22 "\\"Sultanat") declined in the 13th century, [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anatolia/%22 "\\"Anatolie\\"") was divided into a patchwork of independent Turkish principalities known as the [Anatolian Beyliks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anatolian_Beyliks/%22 "\\"Beyliks"). One of these, in the region of [Bithynia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bithynia/%22 "\\"Bithynie\\"") on the frontier of the [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Byzantine_Empire/%22 "\\"Empire"), was led by the Turkish<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-48\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>35<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> tribal leader [Osman I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Osman_I/%22 "\\"Osman") (d. 1323/4),<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-49\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>36<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> a figure of obscure origins from whom the name Ottoman is derived.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-50\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>37<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 444\"="">: 444 </span></sup>  Osman's early followers consisted of Turkish tribal groups and Byzantine renegades, with many but not all converts to Islam.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-51\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>38<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 59\"="">: 59 </span></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-52\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>39<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 127\"="">: 127 </span></sup>  Osman extended control of his principality by conquering Byzantine towns along the [Sakarya River](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sakarya_River/%22 "\\"Rivière"). A Byzantine defeat at the [Battle of Bapheus](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Bapheus/%22 "\\"Bataille") in 1302 contributed to Osman's rise. It is not well understood how the early Ottomans came to dominate their neighbors, due to the lack of sources surviving. The [Ghaza thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ghaza_thesis/%22 "\\"Thèse") popular during the 20th century credited their success to rallying religious warriors to fight for them in the name of [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Islam/%22 "\\"Islam\\""), but it is no longer generally accepted. No other hypothesis has attracted broad acceptance.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-53\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>40<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 5,="" 10\"="">: 5, 10 </span></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-54\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>41<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 104\"="">: 104 </span></sup> \\n

In the century after Osman I, Ottoman rule had begun to extend over Anatolia and the [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_the_Balkans/%22 "\\"Histoire"). The earliest conflicts began during the [Byzantine–Ottoman wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars/%22 "\\"Guerres"), waged in Anatolia in the late 13th century before entering Europe in the mid-14th century, followed by the [Bulgarian–Ottoman wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bulgarian%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars/%22 "\\"Guerres") and the [Serbian–Ottoman wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Serbian%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars/%22 "\\"Guerres") in the mid-14th century. Much of this period was characterised by [Ottoman expansion into the Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rumelia/%22 "\\"Roumélie\\""). Osman's son, [Orhan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Orhan/%22 "\\"Orhan\\""), captured the northwestern Anatolian city of [Bursa](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bursa/%22 "\\"Bursa\\"") in 1326, making it the new capital and supplanting Byzantine control in the region. The important port of [Thessaloniki](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Thessaloniki/%22 "\\"Thessalonique\\"") was captured from the [Venetians](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Republic_of_Venice/%22 "\\"République") in 1387 and sacked. The Ottoman victory in [Kosovo in 1389](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo/%22 "\\"Bataille") effectively marked the [end of Serbian power](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Fall_of_the_Serbian_Empire/%22 "\\"Chute") in the region, paving the way for Ottoman expansion into Europe.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-55\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>42<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 95–96\"="">: 95–96 </span></sup>  The [Battle of Nicopolis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis/%22 "\\"Bataille") for the [Bulgarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire/%22 "\\"Second") [Tsardom of Vidin](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tsardom_of_Vidin/%22 "\\"Tsarat") in 1396, regarded as the last large-scale [crusade](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crusades/%22 "\\"Croisades\\"") of the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Middle_Ages/%22 "\\"Moyen-âge\\""), failed to stop the advance of the victorious Ottomans.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-56\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>43<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/250px-Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/%22)

The [Battle of Nicopolis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis/%22 "\\"Bataille") in 1396, as depicted in an [Ottoman miniature](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_miniature/%22 "\\"Miniature") from 1523

\\n

As the Turks expanded into the Balkans, the [conquest of Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sieges_of_Constantinople#Ottoman_Sieges\%22 "\\"Sièges") became a crucial objective. The Ottomans had already wrested control of nearly all former Byzantine lands surrounding the city, but the strong defense of Constantinople's strategic position on the [Bosporus](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bosporus/%22 "\\"Bosphore\\"") Strait made it difficult to conquer. In 1402, the Byzantines were temporarily relieved when the [Turco-Mongol](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turco-Mongol/%22 "\\"turco-mongol\\"") leader [Timur](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Timur/%22 "\\"Timur\\""), founder of the [Timurid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Timurid_Empire/%22 "\\"Empire"), invaded Ottoman Anatolia from the east. In the [Battle of Ankara](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Ankara/%22 "\\"Bataille") in 1402, Timur defeated Ottoman forces and took Sultan [Bayezid I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bayezid_I/%22 "\\"Bayezid") as prisoner, throwing the empire into disorder. The [ensuing civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Interregnum/%22 "\\"Interrègne") lasted from 1402 to 1413 as Bayezid's sons fought over succession. It ended when [Mehmed I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_I/%22 "\\"Mehmed") emerged as the sultan and restored Ottoman power.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-57\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>44<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 363\"="">: 363 </span></sup> \\n

The Balkan territories lost by the Ottomans after 1402, including Thessaloniki, Macedonia, and Kosovo, were later recovered by [Murad II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Murad_II/%22 "\\"Murad") between the 1430s and 1450s. On 10 November 1444, Murad repelled the [Crusade of Varna](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crusade_of_Varna/%22 "\\"Croisade") by defeating the Hungarian, Polish, and [Wallachian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wallachia/%22 "\\"Valachie\\"") armies under [Władysław III of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland/%22 "\\"Ladislas") and [John Hunyadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/John_Hunyadi/%22 "\\"Jean") at the [Battle of Varna](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Varna/%22 "\\"Bataille"), although Albanians under [Skanderbeg](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Skanderbeg/%22 "\\"Skanderbeg\\"") continued to resist. Four years later, John Hunyadi prepared another army of Hungarian and Wallachian forces to attack the Turks, but was again defeated at the [Second Battle of Kosovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo_\(1448\)/%22 "\\"Bataille") in 1448.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-58\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-58\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>45<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 29\"="">: 29 </span></sup> \\n

According to modern historiography, there is a direct connection between the rapid Ottoman military advance and the consequences of the [Black Death](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Black_Death/%22 "\\"peste") from the mid-fourteenth century onwards. Byzantine territories, where the initial Ottoman conquests were carried out, were exhausted demographically and militarily due to the plague, which facilitated Ottoman expansion. In addition, slave hunting was the main economic driving force behind Ottoman conquest. Some 21st-century authors re-periodize conquest of the Balkans into the *akıncı phase*, which spanned 8 to 13 decades, characterized by continuous slave hunting and destruction, followed by administrative integration into the Empire.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Schmitt-Kiprovska_59-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Schmitt-Kiprovska-59\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>46<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Nükhet_Varlik_60-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-N%C3%BCkhet_Varlik-60\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>47<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Ayalon-2014_61-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Ayalon-2014-61\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>48<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-62\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-62\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>49<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

### Expansion and peak (1453–1566)

\\n

Main article: [Classical Age of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Classical_Age_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"L'âge")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/250px-Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/%22)

Sultan [Mehmed the Conqueror](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_II/%22 "\\"Mehmed")'s entry into [Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Constantinople/%22 "\\"Constantinople\\""); painting by [Fausto Zonaro](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Fausto_Zonaro/%22 "\\"Fausto") (1854–1929)

\\n

The son of Murad II, [Mehmed the Conqueror](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror/%22 "\\"Mehmed"), reorganized both state and military, and on 29 May 1453 conquered [Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople/%22 "\\"Chute"), ending the Byzantine Empire.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Quataert2005_63-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Quataert2005-63\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>50<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Mehmed allowed the [Eastern Orthodox Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church/%22 "\\"Église") to maintain its autonomy and land in exchange for accepting Ottoman authority.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_64-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google-64\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>51<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Due to tension between the states of western Europe and the later Byzantine Empire, most of the Orthodox population accepted Ottoman rule, as preferable to Venetian rule.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_64-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google-64\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>51<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Albanian resistance was a major obstacle to Ottoman expansion on the Italian peninsula.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-65\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-65\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>52<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

In the 15th and 16th centuries, the Ottoman Empire entered a [period of expansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Growth_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Croissance"). The Empire prospered under the rule of a line of committed and effective [Sultans](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Dynasty/%22 "\\"Dynastie"). It flourished economically due to its control of the major overland trade routes between Europe and Asia.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-66\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-66\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>53<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 111\"="">: 111 </span></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-67\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-67\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>n<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Sultan [Selim I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Selim_I/%22 "\\"Sélim") (1512–1520) dramatically expanded the eastern and southern frontiers by defeating [Shah Ismail](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ismail_I/%22 "\\"Ismaïl") of [Safavid Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Safavid_Iran/%22 "\\"Iran"), in the [Battle of Chaldiran](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Chaldiran/%22 "\\"Bataille").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-68\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-68\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>54<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" emplacement="" :="" 91–105\"="">: 91–105 </span></sup>  Selim I established [Ottoman rule in Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet/%22 "\\"Égypte") by defeating and annexing the [Mamluk Sultanate of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate/%22 "\\"Sultanat") and created a naval presence on the [Red Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Red_Sea/%22 "\\"mer"). After this Ottoman expansion, competition began between the [Portuguese Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Portuguese_Empire/%22 "\\"Empire") and the Ottomans to become the dominant power in the region.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-69\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-69\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>55<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 55–76\"="">: 55–76 </span></sup> \\n

\\n

[![\"\"](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/EmperorSuleiman.jpg/250px-EmperorSuleiman.jpg/%22)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/File:EmperorSuleiman.jpg/%22)

[![\"\"](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tizian_123.jpg/120px-Tizian_123.jpg/%22)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/File:Tizian_123.jpg/%22)

[Suleiman the Magnificent](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent/%22 "\\"Suleiman") and his wife [Hürrem Sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hurrem_Sultan/%22 "\\"Hurrem"), by 16th century [Venetian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Republic_of_Venice/%22 "\\"Republic") [painter](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Venetian_painting/%22 "\\"Venetian") [Titian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Titian/%22 "\\"Titian\\"")

\\n

[Suleiman the Magnificent](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent/%22 "\\"Suleiman") (1520–1566)<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-70\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-70\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>56<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> captured [Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Belgrade/%22 "\\"Belgrade\\"") in 1521, conquered the southern and central parts of the [Kingdom of Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary/%22 "\\"Kingdom") as part of the [Ottoman–Hungarian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Hungarian_Wars/%22 "\\"Ottoman–Hungarian"), and, after his historic victory in the [Battle of Mohács](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs/%22 "\\"Battle") in 1526, he established Ottoman rule in the territory of present-day Hungary and other Central European territories. He then laid [siege to Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Vienna_\(1529\)/%22 "\\"Siege") in 1529, but failed to take the city.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-71\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-71\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>57<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 50\"="">: 50 </span></sup>  In 1532, he made another [attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Habsburg%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars_in_Hungary_\(1526%E2%80%931568\)/%22 "\\"Habsburg–Ottoman") on Vienna, but was repulsed in the [siege of Güns](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_G%C3%BCns/%22 "\\"Siege").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Thompson442_72-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Thompson442-72\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>58<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Ágoston_and_Alan_Masters583_73-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22%C3%81goston_and_Alan_Masters583-73\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>59<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> [Transylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Transylvania/%22 "\\"Transylvania\\""), Wallachia and, intermittently, [Moldavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Moldavia/%22 "\\"Moldavia\\""), became tributary principalities of the Empire. In the east, the Ottoman Turks [took](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Safavid_War_\(1532%E2%80%931555\)/%22 "\\"Ottoman–Safavid") [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Baghdad/%22 "\\"Baghdad\\"") from the Persians in 1535, gaining control of [Mesopotamia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mesopotamia/%22 "\\"Mesopotamia\\"") and naval access to the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Persian_Gulf/%22 "\\"Persian"). In 1555, the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caucasus/%22 "\\"Caucasus\\"") became partitioned for the first time between the Safavids and the Ottomans, a *[status quo](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Status_quo/%22 "\\"Status")* that remained until the end of the [Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1768%E2%80%931774\)/%22 "\\"Russo-Turkish"). By this partitioning as signed in the [Peace of Amasya](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Peace_of_Amasya/%22 "\\"Peace"), [Western Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Western_Armenia/%22 "\\"Western"), western [Kurdistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kurdistan/%22 "\\"Kurdistan\\""), and [Western Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kingdom_of_Imereti/%22 "\\"Kingdom") fell into Ottoman hands,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-74\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-74\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>60<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> while southern [Dagestan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dagestan/%22 "\\"Dagestan\\""), [Eastern Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Eastern_Armenia/%22 "\\"Eastern"), [Eastern Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Eastern_Georgia_\(country\)/%22 "\\"Eastern"), and [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Azerbaijan/%22 "\\"Azerbaijan\\"") remained Persian.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-75\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-75\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>61<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg/250px-Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg/%22)

Ottoman miniature of the [Battle of Mohács](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs/%22 "\\"Battle") in 1526<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-76\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-76\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>62<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>

\\n

In 1539, a 60,000-strong Ottoman army besieged the [Spanish](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Habsburg_Spain/%22 "\\"Habsburg") garrison of [Castelnuovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Castelnuovo/%22 "\\"Siege") on the [Adriatic coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Adriatic_coast/%22 "\\"Adriatic"); the successful siege cost the Ottomans 8,000 casualties,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-77\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-77\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>63<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> but [Venice](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Republic_of_Venice/%22 "\\"Republic") agreed to terms in 1540, surrendering most of its empire in the [Aegean](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Aegean_Sea/%22 "\\"Aegean") and the [Morea](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Morea/%22 "\\"Morea\\""). [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Early_Modern_France/%22 "\\"Early") and the Ottoman Empire, united by mutual opposition to [Habsburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Habsburg/%22 "\\"Habsburg\\"") rule,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-AksanOW_78-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-AksanOW-78\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>64<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> became allies. The French conquests of [Nice](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Nice/%22 "\\"Siege") (1543) and [Corsica](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Invasion_of_Corsica_\(1553\)/%22 "\\"Invasion") (1553) occurred as a joint venture between French king [Francis I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Francis_I_of_France/%22 "\\"Francis") and Suleiman, and were commanded by the Ottoman admirals [Hayreddin Barbarossa](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa/%22 "\\"Hayreddin") and [Dragut](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dragut/%22 "\\"Dragut\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-79\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-79\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>65<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> France supported the Ottomans with an artillery unit during the 1543 Ottoman [conquest of Esztergom](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Esztergom_\(1543\)/%22 "\\"Siege") in northern Hungary. After further advances by the Turks, the Habsburg ruler [Ferdinand](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor/%22 "\\"Ferdinand") officially recognized Ottoman ascendancy in Hungary in 1547. Suleiman died of natural causes during the [siege of Szigetvár](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Szigetv%C3%A1r/%22 "\\"Siege") in 1566. Following his death, the Ottomans were said to be declining, although this has been rejected by many scholars.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-decline_80-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-decline-80\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>66<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> By the end of Suleiman's reign, the Empire spanned approximately 877,888 sq mi (2,273,720 km<sup>2</sup>), extending over three continents.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-81\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-81\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>67<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 545\"="">: 545 </span></sup> \\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/IAN_0137_Urrabieta_y_Ortiz_1859_Preveza.jpg/250px-IAN_0137_Urrabieta_y_Ortiz_1859_Preveza.jpg/%22)

Ottoman admiral [Barbarossa Hayreddin Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa/%22 "\\"Hayreddin") defeated the [Holy League](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Holy_League_\(1538\)/%22 "\\"Holy") of [Charles V](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor/%22 "\\"Charles") under the command of [Andrea Doria](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Andrea_Doria/%22 "\\"Andrea") at the [Battle of Preveza](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Preveza/%22 "\\"Battle") in 1538.

\\n

The Empire became a dominant naval force, controlling much of the [Mediterranean Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea/%22 "\\"Mediterranean").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-82\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-82\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>68<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 61\"="">: 61 </span></sup>  The Empire was now a major part of European politics. The Ottomans became involved in multi-continental religious wars when Spain and Portugal were united under the [Iberian Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Iberian_Union/%22 "\\"Iberian"). The Ottomans were holders of the Caliph title, meaning they were the leaders of Muslims worldwide. The Iberians were leaders of the Christian crusaders, and so the two fought in a worldwide conflict. There were zones of operations in the Mediterranean<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-83\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-83\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>69<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and [Indian Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Indian_Ocean/%22 "\\"Indian"),<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-84\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-84\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>70<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> where Iberians circumnavigated Africa to reach India and, on their way, wage war upon the Ottomans and their local Muslim allies. Likewise, the Iberians passed through newly-Christianized [Latin America](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Latin_America/%22 "\\"Latin") and [had sent expeditions](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Juan_de_Salcedo/%22 "\\"Juan") that traversed the Pacific to Christianize the formerly Muslim Philippines and use it as a base to attack the Muslims in the [Far East](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Far_East/%22 "\\"Far").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-85\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-85\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>71<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In this case, the Ottomans sent armies to aid its easternmost vassal and territory, the [Sultanate of Aceh](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sultanate_of_Aceh/%22 "\\"Sultanate") in Southeast Asia.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-86\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-86\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>72<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 84\"="">: 84 </span></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-87\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-87\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>73<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

During the 1600s, the world conflict between the Ottoman Caliphate and Iberian Union was a stalemate since [both were at similar population](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_in_1600/%22 "\\"List"), technology and economic levels. Nevertheless, the success of the Ottoman political and military establishment was compared to the [Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Roman_Empire/%22 "\\"Roman"), despite the difference in size, by the likes of contemporary Italian scholar [Francesco Sansovino](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Francesco_Sansovino/%22 "\\"Francesco") and French political philosopher [Jean Bodin](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Jean_Bodin/%22 "\\"Jean").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-deringil709_88-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-deringil709-88\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>74<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

### Stagnation and reform (1566–1827)

\\n

#### Revolts, reversals, and revivals (1566–1683)

\\n

Main article: [Transformation of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Transformation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Transformation")

\\n

Further information: [Ottoman decline thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_decline_thesis/%22 "\\"Ottoman")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/IstanbulNavalMuseum38.JPG/250px-IstanbulNavalMuseum38.JPG/%22)

Late 16th or early 17th century [Ottoman](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Navy/%22 "\\"Ottoman") [galley](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Galley/%22 "\\"Galley\\"") known as *[Tarihi Kadırga](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tarihi_Kad%C4%B1rga/%22 "\\"Tarihi")* at the [Istanbul Naval Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Istanbul_Naval_Museum/%22 "\\"Istanbul"), built in the period between the reigns of Sultan [Murad III](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Murad_III/%22 "\\"Murad") (1574–1595) and Sultan [Mehmed IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_IV/%22 "\\"Mehmed") (1648–1687)<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-kadirga1_89-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-kadirga1-89\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>75<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-kadirga2_90-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-kadirga2-90\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>76<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>

\\n

In the second half of the sixteenth century, the Ottoman Empire came under increasing strain from inflation and the rapidly rising costs of warfare that were impacting both Europe and the Middle East.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-91\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-91\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>77<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> These pressures led to a series of crises around the year 1600, placing great strain upon the Ottoman system of government.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-92\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-92\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>78<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 413–414\"="">: 413–414 </span></sup>  The empire underwent a series of transformations of its political and military institutions in response to these challenges, enabling it to successfully adapt to the new conditions of the seventeenth century and remain powerful, both militarily and economically.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-decline_80-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-decline-80\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>66<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-93\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-93\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>79<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 10\"="">: 10 </span></sup>  Historians of the mid-twentieth century once characterised this period as one of stagnation and decline, but this view is now rejected by the majority of academics.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-decline_80-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-decline-80\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>66<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The discovery of new maritime trade routes by Western European states allowed them to avoid the Ottoman trade monopoly. The [Portuguese](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal/%22 "\\"Kingdom") discovery of the [Cape of Good Hope](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope/%22 "\\"Cape") in 1488 initiated [a series of Ottoman-Portuguese naval wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_naval_expeditions_in_the_Indian_Ocean/%22 "\\"Ottoman") in the [Indian Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Indian_Ocean/%22 "\\"Indian") throughout the 16th century. Despite the growing European presence in the Indian Ocean, Ottoman trade with the east continued to flourish. Cairo, in particular, benefitted from the rise of Yemeni coffee as a popular consumer commodity. As coffeehouses appeared in cities and towns across the empire, Cairo developed into a major center for its trade, contributing to its continued prosperity throughout the seventeenth and much of the eighteenth century.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-94\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-94\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>80<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 507–508\"="">: 507–508 </span></sup> \\n

Under [Ivan IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ivan_IV/%22 "\\"Ivan") (1533–1584), the [Tsardom of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia/%22 "\\"Tsardom") expanded into the Volga and Caspian regions at the expense of the Tatar khanates. In 1571, the Crimean khan [Devlet I Giray](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Devlet_I_Giray/%22 "\\"Devlet"), commanded by the Ottomans, [burned Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Fire_of_Moscow_\(1571\)/%22 "\\"Fire").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Davies2007_95-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Davies2007-95\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>81<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The next year, the invasion was repeated but repelled at the [Battle of Molodi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Molodi/%22 "\\"Battle"). The Ottoman Empire continued to invade Eastern Europe in a series of [slave raids](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/List_of_conflicts_in_Europe_during_Turco-Mongol_rule/%22 "\\"List"),<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Subtelny2000_96-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Subtelny2000-96\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>82<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and remained a significant power in Eastern Europe until the end of the 17th century.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-97\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-97\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>83<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Giorgio-vasari-battle-of-lepanto.jpg/250px-Giorgio-vasari-battle-of-lepanto.jpg/%22)

Order of battle of the two fleets in the [Battle of Lepanto](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto/%22 "\\"Battle"), with an allegory of the three powers of the [Holy League](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Holy_League_\(1571\)/%22 "\\"Holy") in the foreground, fresco by [Giorgio Vasari](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Giorgio_Vasari/%22 "\\"Giorgio")

\\n

The Ottomans decided to conquer [Venetian Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Venetian_Cyprus/%22 "\\"Venetian") and on 22 July 1570, Nicosia was besieged; 50,000 Christians died, and 180,000 were enslaved.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-98\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-98\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>84<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 67\"="">: 67 </span></sup>  On 15 September 1570, the Ottoman cavalry appeared before the last Venetian stronghold in Cyprus, Famagusta. The Venetian defenders held out for 11 months against a force that at its peak numbered 200,000 men with 145 cannons; 163,000 cannonballs struck the walls of Famagusta before it fell to the Ottomans in August 1571. The [Siege of Famagusta](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Famagusta/%22 "\\"Siege") claimed 50,000 Ottoman casualties.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-99\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-99\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>85<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 328\"="">: 328 </span></sup>  Meanwhile, the [Holy League](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Holy_League_\(1571\)/%22 "\\"Holy") consisting of mostly Spanish and Venetian fleets won a victory over the Ottoman fleet at the [Battle of Lepanto](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto/%22 "\\"Battle") (1571), off southwestern Greece; Catholic forces killed over 30,000 Turks and destroyed 200 of their ships.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-100\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-100\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>86<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 24\"="">: 24 </span></sup>  It was a startling, if mostly symbolic,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979272_101-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979272-101\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>87<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> blow to the image of Ottoman invincibility, an image which the victory of the Knights of Malta over the Ottoman invaders in the 1565 [siege of Malta](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Malta/%22 "\\"Great") had recently set about eroding.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-102\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-102\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>88<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The battle was far more damaging to the Ottoman navy in sapping experienced manpower than the loss of ships, which were rapidly replaced.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-103\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-103\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>89<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 53\"="">: 53 </span></sup>  The Ottoman navy recovered quickly, persuading Venice to sign a peace treaty in 1573, allowing the Ottomans to expand and consolidate their position in North Africa.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198067_104-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198067-104\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>90<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

By contrast, the Habsburg frontier had settled somewhat, a stalemate caused by a stiffening of the Habsburg defenses.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198071_105-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198071-105\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>91<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The [Long Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Long_Turkish_War/%22 "\\"Long") against Habsburg Austria (1593–1606) created the need for greater numbers of Ottoman infantry equipped with firearms, resulting in a relaxation of recruitment policy. This contributed to problems of indiscipline and outright rebelliousness within the corps, which were never fully solved.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198090–92_106-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198090%E2%80%9392-106\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>92<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;noprint" inline-template="" noprint="" template-fact\"="" style="\&quot;white-space:nowrap;\&quot;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wikipedia:AGE_MATTERS/%22" class="\&quot;mw-redirect\&quot;" title="\&quot;Wikipedia:AGE" matters\"=""><span title="\&quot;This" claim="" needs="" references="" to="" more="" current="" sources.="" (september="" 2016)\"="">obsolete&nbsp;source</span></a></i>]</sup> Irregular sharpshooters ([Sekban](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sekban/%22 "\\"Sekban\\"")) were also recruited, and on demobilisation turned to [brigandage](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Brigandage/%22 "\\"Brigandage\\"") in the [Celali rebellions](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Celali_rebellions/%22 "\\"Celali") (1590–1610), which engendered widespread anarchy in [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anatolia/%22 "\\"Anatolia\\"") in the late 16th and early 17th centuries.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-107\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-107\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>93<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 24\"="">: 24 </span></sup>  With the Empire's population reaching 30 million people by 1600, the shortage of land placed further pressure on the government.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281_108-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281-108\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>94<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;noprint" inline-template="" noprint="" template-fact\"="" style="\&quot;white-space:nowrap;\&quot;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wikipedia:AGE_MATTERS/%22" class="\&quot;mw-redirect\&quot;" title="\&quot;Wikipedia:AGE" matters\"=""><span title="\&quot;This" claim="" needs="" references="" to="" more="" current="" sources.="" (september="" 2016)\"="">obsolete&nbsp;source</span></a></i>]</sup> In spite of these problems, the Ottoman state remained strong, and its army did not collapse or suffer crushing defeats. The only exceptions were campaigns against the [Safavid dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Safavid_dynasty/%22 "\\"Safavid") of Persia, where many of the Ottoman eastern provinces were lost, some permanently. This [1603–1618 war](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Safavid_War_\(1603%E2%80%931618\)/%22 "\\"Ottoman–Safavid") eventually resulted in the [Treaty of Nasuh Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_Nasuh_Pasha/%22 "\\"Treaty"), which ceded the entire Caucasus, except westernmost Georgia, back into the possession of [Safavid Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Safavid_Iran/%22 "\\"Safavid").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-109\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-109\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>95<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The treaty ending the [Cretan War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Cretan_War_\(1645%E2%80%931669\)/%22 "\\"Cretan") cost Venice much of [Dalmatia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Venetian_Dalmatia/%22 "\\"Venetian"), its Aegean island possessions, and [Crete](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kingdom_of_Candia/%22 "\\"Kingdom"). (Losses from the war totalled 30,985 Venetian soldiers and 118,754 Turkish soldiers.)<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-110\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-110\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>96<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 33\"="">: 33 </span></sup> \\n

During his brief majority reign, [Murad IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Murad_IV/%22 "\\"Murad") (1623–1640) reasserted central authority and recaptured [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Iraq/%22 "\\"Iraq\\"") (1639) from the Safavids.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198073_111-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198073-111\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>97<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The resulting [Treaty of Zuhab](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_Zuhab/%22 "\\"Treaty") of that same year decisively divided the Caucasus and adjacent regions between the two neighbouring empires as it had already been defined in the 1555 Peace of Amasya.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-112\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-112\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>98<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-113\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-113\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>99<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The [Sultanate of Women](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sultanate_of_Women/%22 "\\"Sultanate") (1533–1656) was a period in which the mothers of young sultans exercised power on behalf of their sons. The most prominent women of this period were [Kösem Sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/K%C3%B6sem_Sultan/%22 "\\"Kösem") and her daughter-in-law [Turhan Hatice](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turhan_Hatice/%22 "\\"Turhan"), whose political rivalry culminated in Kösem's murder in 1651.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198074–75_114-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198074%E2%80%9375-114\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>100<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> During the [Köprülü era](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/K%C3%B6pr%C3%BCl%C3%BC_era/%22 "\\"Köprülü") (1656–1703), effective control of the Empire was exercised by a sequence of [grand viziers](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Grand_vizier/%22 "\\"Grand") from the Köprülü family. The Köprülü Vizierate saw renewed military success with authority restored in Transylvania, the conquest of [Crete](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crete/%22 "\\"Crete\\"") completed in 1669, and expansion into [Polish southern Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Ukraine#Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth\%22 "\\"History"), with the strongholds of [Khotyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Khotyn/%22 "\\"Khotyn\\""), and [Kamianets-Podilskyi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kamianets-Podilskyi/%22 "\\"Kamianets-Podilskyi\\"") and the territory of [Podolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Podolia/%22 "\\"Podolia\\"") ceding to Ottoman control in 1676.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198080–81_115-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198080%E2%80%9381-115\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>101<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/250px-Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/%22)

The [Second Siege of Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna/%22 "\\"Battle") in 1683, by [Frans Geffels](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Frans_Geffels/%22 "\\"Frans") (1624–1694)

\\n

This period of renewed assertiveness came to a calamitous end in 1683 when Grand Vizier [Kara Mustafa Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kara_Mustafa_Pasha/%22 "\\"Kara") led a huge army to attempt a second Ottoman siege of [Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Vienna/%22 "\\"History") in the [Great Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Great_Turkish_War/%22 "\\"Great") of 1683–1699. The final assault being fatally delayed, the Ottoman forces were swept away by allied Habsburg, German, and Polish forces spearheaded by the Polish king [John III Sobieski](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/John_III_Sobieski/%22 "\\"John") at the [Battle of Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna/%22 "\\"Battle"). The alliance of the [Holy League](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Holy_League_\(1684\)/%22 "\\"Holy") pressed home the advantage of the defeat at Vienna, culminating in the [Treaty of Karlowitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_Karlowitz/%22 "\\"Treaty") (26 January 1699), which ended the Great Turkish War.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979357_116-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979357-116\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>102<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Ottomans surrendered control of significant territories, many permanently.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198084_117-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198084-117\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>103<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> [Mustafa II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mustafa_II/%22 "\\"Mustafa") (1695–1703) led the counterattack of 1695–1696 against the Habsburgs in Hungary, but was undone at the disastrous defeat at [Zenta](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Zenta/%22 "\\"Battle") (in modern Serbia), 11 September 1697.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198083–84_118-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198083%E2%80%9384-118\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>104<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

#### Military defeats

\\n

Aside from the loss of the [Banat](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Banat/%22 "\\"Banat\\"") and the temporary loss of [Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Belgrade/%22 "\\"History") (1717–1739), the Ottoman border on the [Danube](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Danube/%22 "\\"Danube\\"") and [Sava](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sava/%22 "\\"Sava\\"") remained stable during the eighteenth century. [Russian expansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Expansion_of_Russia_1500%E2%80%931800/%22 "\\"Expansion"), however, presented a large and growing threat.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371_119-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371-119\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>105<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Accordingly, King [Charles XII of Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Charles_XII_of_Sweden/%22 "\\"Charles") was welcomed as an ally in the Ottoman Empire following his defeat by the Russians at the [Battle of Poltava](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Poltava/%22 "\\"Battle") of 1709 in central Ukraine (part of the [Great Northern War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Great_Northern_War/%22 "\\"Great") of 1700–1721).<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371_119-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371-119\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>105<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Charles XII persuaded the Ottoman Sultan [Ahmed III](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ahmed_III/%22 "\\"Ahmed") to declare war on Russia, which resulted in an Ottoman victory in the [Pruth River Campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Pruth_River_Campaign/%22 "\\"Pruth") of 1710–1711, in Moldavia.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979372_120-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979372-120\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>106<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/250px-1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/%22)

Austrian troops led by [Prince Eugene of Savoy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Prince_Eugene_of_Savoy/%22 "\\"Prince") capture [Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Belgrade/%22 "\\"Belgrade\\"") in 1717. Austrian control in Serbia lasted until the Turkish victory in the [Austro-Russian–Turkish War (1735–1739)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1735%E2%80%931739\)/%22 "\\"Russo-Turkish"). With the 1739 [Treaty of Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_Belgrade/%22 "\\"Treaty"), the Ottoman Empire regained northern [Bosnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina/%22 "\\"Bosnia"), [Habsburg Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_\(1718%E2%80%931739\)/%22 "\\"Kingdom") (including Belgrade), [Oltenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Oltenia/%22 "\\"Oltenia\\"") and the southern parts of the [Banat of Temeswar](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Banat_of_Temeswar/%22 "\\"Banat").

\\n

After the [Austro-Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_\(1716%E2%80%931718\)/%22 "\\"Austro-Turkish"), the [Treaty of Passarowitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_Passarowitz/%22 "\\"Treaty") confirmed the loss of the Banat, Serbia, and [\\"Little Walachia\\" (Oltenia)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Oltenia/%22 "\\"Oltenia\\"") to Austria. The Treaty also revealed that the Ottoman Empire was on the defensive and unlikely to present any further aggression in Europe.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979376_121-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979376-121\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>107<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The [Austro-Russian–Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Austro-Russian%E2%80%93Turkish_War_\(1735%E2%80%931739\)/%22 "\\"Austro-Russian–Turkish") (1735–1739), which was ended by the [Treaty of Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_Belgrade/%22 "\\"Treaty") in 1739, resulted in the Ottoman recovery of northern [Bosnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bosnia/%22 "\\"Bosnia\\""), [Habsburg Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_\(1718%E2%80%931739\)/%22 "\\"Kingdom") (including Belgrade), [Oltenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Oltenia/%22 "\\"Oltenia\\"") and the southern parts of the [Banat of Temeswar](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Banat_of_Temeswar/%22 "\\"Banat"); but the Empire lost the port of [Azov](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Azov/%22 "\\"Azov\\""), north of the Crimean Peninsula, to the Russians. After this treaty the Ottoman Empire was able to enjoy a generation of peace in Europe, as Austria and Russia were forced to deal with the rise of [Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Prussia/%22 "\\"Prussia\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979392_122-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979392-122\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>108<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

[Educational and technological reforms](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Science_and_Technology_in_the_Ottoman_Empire#Education\%22 "\\"Science") came about, including the establishment of higher education institutions such as the [Istanbul Technical University](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Istanbul_Technical_University/%22 "\\"Istanbul").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-123\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-123\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>109<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1734 an artillery school was established to impart Western-style artillery methods, but the Islamic clergy successfully objected under the grounds of
