[theodicy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Theodicy/%22 "\\"Theodicy\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_a_124-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_a-124\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>110<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1754 the artillery school was reopened on a semi-secret basis.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_a_124-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_a-124\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>110<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1726, [Ibrahim Muteferrika](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ibrahim_Muteferrika/%22 "\\"Ibrahim") convinced the Grand Vizier [Nevşehirli Damat Ibrahim Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Nev%C5%9Fehirli_Damat_Ibrahim_Pasha/%22 "\\"Nevşehirli"), the [Grand Mufti](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Grand_Mufti/%22 "\\"Grand"), and the clergy on the efficiency of the printing press, and Muteferrika was later granted by Sultan Ahmed III permission to publish non-religious books (despite opposition from some [calligraphers](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Islamic_calligraphy/%22 "\\"Islamic") and religious leaders).<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-katip_celebi_125-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-katip_celebi-125\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>111<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Muteferrika's press published its first book in 1729 and, by 1743, issued 17 works in 23 volumes, each having between 500 and 1,000 copies.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-katip_celebi_125-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-katip_celebi-125\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>111<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-watson_126-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-watson-126\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>112<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

In North Africa, Spain [conquered Oran](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Oran_\(1732\)/%22 "\\"Spanish") from the autonomous [Deylik of Algiers](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Deylik_of_Algiers/%22 "\\"Deylik"). The [Bey of Oran](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Beylik_of_Oran/%22 "\\"Beylik") received an army from Algiers, but it failed to recapture [Oran](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Oran/%22 "\\"Oran\\""); the siege caused the deaths of 1,500 Spaniards, and even more Algerians. The Spanish also massacred many Muslim soldiers.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-127\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-127\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>113<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1792, Spain abandoned Oran, selling it to the Deylik of Algiers.\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/220px-January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/%22)

Ottoman troops attempting to halt the advancing Russians during the [Siege of Ochakov](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Ochakov_\(1788\)/%22 "\\"Siege") in 1788

\\n

In 1768 Russian-backed Ukrainian [Haidamakas](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Haidamaka/%22 "\\"Haidamaka\\""), pursuing Polish confederates, entered [Balta](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Balta,_Ukraine/%22 "\\"Balta,"), an Ottoman-controlled town on the border of Bessarabia in Ukraine, massacred its citizens, and burned the town to the ground. This action provoked the Ottoman Empire into the [Russo-Turkish War of 1768–1774](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1768%E2%80%931774\)/%22 "\\"Russo-Turkish"). The [Treaty of Küçük Kaynarca](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Kaynarca/%22 "\\"Treaty") of 1774 ended the war and provided freedom of worship for the Christian citizens of the Ottoman-controlled provinces of Wallachia and Moldavia.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979405_128-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979405-128\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>114<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> By the late 18th century, after a number of defeats in the wars with Russia, some people in the Ottoman Empire began to conclude that the reforms of [Peter the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Peter_the_Great/%22 "\\"Peter") had given the Russians an edge, and the Ottomans would have to keep up with Western technology in order to avoid further defeats.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_a_124-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_a-124\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>110<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/250px-Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/%22)

[Selim III](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Selim_III/%22 "\\"Selim") receiving dignitaries during an audience at the Gate of Felicity, [Topkapı Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace/%22 "\\"Topkapı"). Painting by [Konstantin Kapıdağlı](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Konstantin_Kap%C4%B1da%C4%9Fl%C4%B1/%22 "\\"Konstantin")

\\n

[Selim III](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Selim_III/%22 "\\"Selim") (1789–1807) made the first major attempts to [modernise the army](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_military_reform_efforts/%22 "\\"Ottoman"), but his reforms were hampered by the religious leadership and the [Janissary](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Janissary/%22 "\\"Janissary\\"") corps. Jealous of their privileges and firmly opposed to change, the Janissary [revolted](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Janissary_revolts/%22 "\\"Janissary"). Selim's efforts cost him his throne and his life, but were resolved in spectacular and bloody fashion by his successor, the dynamic [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mahmud_II/%22 "\\"Mahmud"), who [eliminated the Janissary corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Auspicious_Incident/%22 "\\"Auspicious") in 1826.\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Gen%C3%A8ve_et_Gr%C3%A8ce_-_Bataille_de_l%27Acropole_par_JGC_Perlberg.jpg/250px-Gen%C3%A8ve_et_Gr%C3%A8ce_-_Bataille_de_l%27Acropole_par_JGC_Perlberg.jpg/%22)

The siege of the Acropolis in 1826–1827 during the [Greek War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence/%22 "\\"Greek")

\\n

The [Serbian revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Serbian_revolution/%22 "\\"Serbian") (1804–1815) marked the beginning of an era of [national awakening](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_under_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Rise") in the [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Balkans/%22 "\\"Balkans\\"") during the [Eastern Question](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Eastern_Question/%22 "\\"Eastern"). In 1811, the fundamentalist Wahhabis of Arabia, led by the al-Saud family, revolted against the Ottomans. Unable to defeat the Wahhabi rebels, the Sublime Porte had [Muhammad Ali Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt/%22 "\\"Muhammad") of [Kavala](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kavala/%22 "\\"Kavala\\""), the *[vali](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wali/%22 "\\"Wali\\"")* (governor) of the [Eyalet of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet/%22 "\\"Egypt"), tasked with retaking Arabia, which ended with the destruction of the [Emirate of Diriyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Emirate_of_Diriyah/%22 "\\"Emirate") in 1818. The [suzerainty](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Suzerainty/%22 "\\"Suzerainty\\"") of Serbia as a hereditary monarchy under its own [dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Obrenovi%C4%87_dynasty/%22 "\\"Obrenović") was acknowledged *[de jure](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/De_jure/%22 "\\"De")* in 1830.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-129\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-129\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>115<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Berend2003_130-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Berend2003-130\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>116<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1821, the [Greeks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Greece/%22 "\\"Ottoman") [declared war](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence/%22 "\\"Greek") on the Sultan. A rebellion that originated in Moldavia as a diversion was followed by the main revolution in the [Peloponnese](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Peloponnese/%22 "\\"Peloponnese\\""), which, along with the northern part of the [Gulf of Corinth](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Gulf_of_Corinth/%22 "\\"Gulf"), became the first parts of the Ottoman Empire to achieve independence (in 1829). In 1830, the French invaded the [Deylik of Algiers](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Deylik_of_Algiers/%22 "\\"Deylik"). [The campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Invasion_of_Algiers_in_1830/%22 "\\"Invasion") that took 21 days, resulted in over 5,000 Algerian military casualties,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-De_Quatrebarbes-1831_131-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-De_Quatrebarbes-1831-131\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>117<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and about 2,600 French ones.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-De_Quatrebarbes-1831_131-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-De_Quatrebarbes-1831-131\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>117<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-132\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-132\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>118<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Before the French invasion the total population of Algeria was most likely between 3,000,000 and 5,000,000.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-133\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-133\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>119<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> By 1873, the population of Algeria (excluding several hundred thousand newly arrived French settlers) had decreased to 2,172,000.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-134\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-134\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>120<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1831, [Muhammad Ali of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt/%22 "\\"Muhammad") revolted against Sultan [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mahmud_II/%22 "\\"Mahmud") due to the latter's refusal to grant him the governorships of [Greater Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Syria_\(region\)/%22 "\\"Syria") and [Crete](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crete/%22 "\\"Crete\\""), which the Sultan had promised him in exchange for sending military assistance to put down the [Greek revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence/%22 "\\"Greek") (1821–1829) that ultimately ended with the formal [independence of Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/London_Protocol_\(1830\)/%22 "\\"London") in 1830. It was a costly enterprise for Muhammad Ali, who had lost his fleet at the [Battle of Navarino](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Navarino/%22 "\\"Battle") in 1827. Thus began the first [Egyptian–Ottoman War (1831–1833)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Egyptian%E2%80%93Ottoman_War_\(1831%E2%80%931833\)/%22 "\\"Egyptian–Ottoman"), during which the French-trained army of Muhammad Ali, under the command of his son [Ibrahim Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ibrahim_Pasha_of_Egypt/%22 "\\"Ibrahim"), defeated the Ottoman Army as it marched into [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anatolia/%22 "\\"Anatolia\\""), reaching the city of [Kütahya](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/K%C3%BCtahya/%22 "\\"Kütahya\\"") within 320 km (200 mi) of the capital, Constantinople.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Effraim_135-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Effraim-135\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>121<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 95\"="">: 95 </span></sup>  In desperation, Sultan [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mahmud_II/%22 "\\"Mahmud") appealed to the empire's traditional arch-rival Russia for help, asking Emperor [Nicholas I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia/%22 "\\"Nicholas") to send an expeditionary force to assist him.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Effraim_135-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Effraim-135\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>121<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 96\"="">: 96 </span></sup>  In return for signing the [Treaty of Hünkâr İskelesi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_H%C3%BCnk%C3%A2r_%C4%B0skelesi/%22 "\\"Treaty"), the Russians sent the expeditionary force which deterred Ibrahim Pasha from marching any further towards Constantinople.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Effraim_135-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Effraim-135\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>121<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 96\"="">: 96 </span></sup>  Under the terms of the [Convention of Kütahya](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Convention_of_K%C3%BCtahya/%22 "\\"Convention"), signed on 5 May 1833, Muhammad Ali agreed to abandon his campaign against the Sultan, in exchange for which he was made the *[vali](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wali/%22 "\\"Wali\\"")* (governor) of the *[vilayets](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Vilayet/%22 "\\"Vilayet\\"")* (provinces) of [Crete](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crete/%22 "\\"Crete\\""), [Aleppo](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Aleppo/%22 "\\"Aleppo\\""), [Tripoli](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tripoli,_Lebanon/%22 "\\"Tripoli,"), [Damascus](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Damascus/%22 "\\"Damascus\\"") and [Sidon](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sidon/%22 "\\"Sidon\\"") (the latter four comprising modern [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Syria/%22 "\\"Syria\\"") and [Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Lebanon/%22 "\\"Lebanon\\"")), and given the right to collect taxes in [Adana](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Adana/%22 "\\"Adana\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Effraim_135-3\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Effraim-135\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>121<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 96\"="">: 96 </span></sup>  Had it not been for the Russian intervention, Sultan [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mahmud_II/%22 "\\"Mahmud") could have faced the risk of being overthrown and Muhammad Ali could have even become the new Sultan. These events marked the beginning of a recurring pattern where the Sublime Porte needed the help of foreign powers to protect itself.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Effraim_135-4\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Effraim-135\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>121<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 95–96\"="">: 95–96 </span></sup> \\n

In 1839, the [Sublime Porte](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sublime_Porte/%22 "\\"Sublime") attempted to take back what it lost to the *[de facto](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/De_facto/%22 "\\"De")* autonomous, but *[de jure](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/De_jure/%22 "\\"De")* still Ottoman [Eyalet of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet/%22 "\\"Egypt"), but its forces were initially defeated, which led to the [Oriental Crisis of 1840](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Oriental_Crisis_of_1840/%22 "\\"Oriental"). Muhammad Ali had close relations with [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/July_Monarchy/%22 "\\"July"), and the prospect of him becoming the Sultan of Egypt was widely viewed as putting the entire [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Levant/%22 "\\"Levant\\"") into the French sphere of influence.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Effraim_135-5\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Effraim-135\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>121<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 96\"="">: 96 </span></sup>  As the Sublime Porte had proved itself incapable of defeating Muhammad Ali,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-136\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-136\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>122<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-137\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-137\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>123<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/British_Empire/%22 "\\"British") and [Austrian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Austrian_Empire/%22 "\\"Austrian") provided military assistance, and the second [Egyptian–Ottoman War (1839–1841)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Egyptian%E2%80%93Ottoman_War_\(1839%E2%80%931841\)/%22 "\\"Egyptian–Ottoman") ended with Ottoman victory and the restoration of Ottoman suzerainty over [Egypt Eyalet](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet/%22 "\\"Egypt") and the [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Levant/%22 "\\"Levant\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Effraim_135-6\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Effraim-135\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>121<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 96\"="">: 96 </span></sup> \\n

By the mid-19th century, the Ottoman Empire was called the \\"[sick man of Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sick_man_of_Europe/%22 "\\"Sick")\\". Three suzerain states – the [Principality of Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia/%22 "\\"Principality"), [Wallachia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wallachia/%22 "\\"Wallachia\\"") and [Moldavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Moldavia/%22 "\\"Moldavia\\"") – moved towards *de jure* independence during the 1860s and 1870s.\\n

\\n

### Decline and modernisation (1828–1908)

\\n

Main article: [Decline of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Decline_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Decline")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Opening_ceremony_of_the_First_Ottoman_Parliament_at_the_Dolmabahce_Palace_in_1876.jpg/250px-Opening_ceremony_of_the_First_Ottoman_Parliament_at_the_Dolmabahce_Palace_in_1876.jpg/%22)

Opening ceremony of the First [Ottoman Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"General") at the [Dolmabahçe Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace/%22 "\\"Dolmabahçe") in 1876. The [First Constitutional Era](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era/%22 "\\"First") lasted only two years until 1878. The Ottoman Constitution and Parliament were [restored 30 years later](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era/%22 "\\"Second") with the [Young Turk Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution/%22 "\\"Young") in 1908.

\\n

During the [Tanzimat](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tanzimat/%22 "\\"Tanzimat\\"") period (1839–1876), the government's series of constitutional reforms led to a fairly modern [conscripted army](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Conscription_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Conscription"), banking system reforms, the decriminalization of homosexuality, the replacement of religious law with secular law,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-138\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-138\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>124<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and guilds with modern factories. The Ottoman Ministry of Post was established in Istanbul in 1840. American inventor [Samuel Morse](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Samuel_Morse/%22 "\\"Samuel") received an Ottoman patent for the telegraph in 1847, issued by Sultan [Abdülmecid](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_I/%22 "\\"Abdülmecid"), who personally tested the invention.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-139\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-139\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>125<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The reformist period peaked with the Constitution, called the *[Kanûn-u Esâsî](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kan%C3%BBn-u_Es%C3%A2s%C3%AE/%22 "\\"Kanûn-u")*. The empire's [First Constitutional era](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era_\(Ottoman_Empire\)/%22 "\\"First") was short-lived. The parliament survived for only two years before the sultan suspended it.\\n

The empire's Christian population, owing to their higher educational levels, started to pull ahead of the Muslim majority, leading to much resentment.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_b_140-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_b-140\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>126<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1861, there were 571 primary and 94 secondary schools for Ottoman Christians, with 140,000 pupils in total, a figure that vastly exceeded the number of Muslim children in school at the time, who were further hindered by the amount of time spent learning Arabic and Islamic theology.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_b_140-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_b-140\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>126<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Author Norman Stone suggests that the Arabic alphabet, in which Turkish was written [until 1928](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkish_alphabet_reform/%22 "\\"Turkish"), was ill-suited to reflect the sounds of Turkish (which is a Turkic as opposed to Semitic language), which imposed further difficulty on Turkish children.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_b_140-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_b-140\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>126<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In turn, Christians' higher educational levels allowed them to play a larger role in the economy, with the rise in prominence of groups such as the [Sursock family](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sursock_family/%22 "\\"Sursock") indicative of this.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-141\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-141\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>127<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_b_140-3\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_b-140\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>126<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1911, of the 654 wholesale companies in Istanbul, 528 were owned by ethnic Greeks.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_b_140-4\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_b-140\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>126<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In many cases, Christians and Jews gained protection from European consuls and citizenship, meaning they were protected from Ottoman law and not subject to the same economic regulations as their Muslim counterparts.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTERogan201193_142-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTERogan201193-142\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>128<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Turkish_troops_storming_Fort_Shefketil_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Turkish_troops_storming_Fort_Shefketil_%28cropped%29.jpg/%22)

Ottoman troops storming [Fort Shefketil](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Shekvetili/%22 "\\"Shekvetili\\"") during the [Crimean War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crimean_War/%22 "\\"Crimean") of 1853–1856

\\n

The [Crimean War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crimean_War/%22 "\\"Crimean") (1853–1856) was part of a long-running contest between the major European powers for influence over territories of the declining Ottoman Empire. The financial burden of the war led the Ottoman state to issue [foreign loans](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_public_debt/%22 "\\"Ottoman") amounting to 5 million pounds sterling on 4 August 1854.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-143\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-143\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>129<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 32\"="">: 32 </span></sup> <sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-144\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-144\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>130<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 71\"="">: 71 </span></sup>  The war caused an exodus of the [Crimean Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crimean_Tatars/%22 "\\"Crimean"), about 200,000 of whom moved to the Ottoman Empire in continuing waves of emigration.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-145\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-145\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>131<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 79–108\"="">: 79–108 </span></sup>  Toward the end of the [Caucasian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caucasian_Wars/%22 "\\"Caucasian"), 90% of the [Circassians](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Circassians/%22 "\\"Circassians\\"") were [ethnically cleansed](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Circassians/%22 "\\"Ethnic")<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-146\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-146\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>132<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and exiled from their homelands in the Caucasus, fleeing to the Ottoman Empire,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-147\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-147\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>133<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> resulting in the settlement of 500,000 to 700,000 Circassians in the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamed-Troyansky202449_148-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamed-Troyansky202449-148\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>134<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Crimean Tatar refugees in the late 19th century played an especially notable role in seeking to modernise Ottoman education and in first promoting both [Pan-Turkism](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Pan-Turkism/%22 "\\"Pan-Turkism\\"") and a sense of Turkish nationalism.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-ReferenceA_149-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-ReferenceA-149\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>135<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Charles_Porion_-_The_kings_of_Europe_in_Paris_for_the_opening_of_the_Exposition_of_1867.jpg/330px-Charles_Porion_-_The_kings_of_Europe_in_Paris_for_the_opening_of_the_Exposition_of_1867.jpg/%22)

The Kings of Europe are in [Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Paris/%22 "\\"Paris\\"") ([Napoleon III](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Napoleon_III/%22 "\\"Napoleon") is at the centre, Sultan [Abdulaziz](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abdulaziz/%22 "\\"Abdulaziz\\"") is second from right) for the opening of the [Universal Exposition of 1867](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Exposition_Universelle_\(1867\)/%22 "\\"Exposition")

\\n

In this period, the Ottoman Empire spent only small amounts of public funds on education; for example, in 1860–1861 only 0.2% of the total budget was invested in education.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-150\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-150\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>136<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 50\"="">: 50 </span></sup>  As the Ottoman state attempted to modernize its infrastructure and army in response to outside threats, it opened itself up to a different kind of threat: that of creditors. As the historian Eugene Rogan has written, \\"the single greatest threat to the independence of the Middle East\\" in the 19th century \\"was not the armies of Europe but its banks\\".<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTERogan2011105_151-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTERogan2011105-151\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>137<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman state, which had begun taking on debt with the Crimean War, was forced to declare bankruptcy in 1875.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTERogan2011106_152-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTERogan2011106-152\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>138<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> By 1881, the Ottoman Empire agreed to have its debt controlled by the [Ottoman Public Debt Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Public_Debt_Administration/%22 "\\"Ottoman"), a council of European men with presidency alternating between France and Britain. The body controlled swaths of the Ottoman economy, and used its position to ensure that European capital continued to penetrate the empire, often to the detriment of local Ottoman interests.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTERogan2011106_152-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTERogan2011106-152\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>138<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Ottomans_1875.png/250px-Ottomans_1875.png/%22)

The Ottoman Empire in 1875 under Sultan [Abdulaziz](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abdulaziz/%22 "\\"Abdulaziz\\"")

\\n

The Ottoman [bashi-bazouks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bashi-bazouk/%22 "\\"Bashi-bazouk\\"") suppressed the [Bulgarian uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/April_Uprising/%22 "\\"April") of 1876, massacring up to 100,000 people in the process.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-153\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-153\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>139<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 139\"="">: 139 </span></sup>  The [Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1877%E2%80%931878\)/%22 "\\"Russo-Turkish") ended with a decisive victory for Russia. As a result, Ottoman holdings in Europe declined sharply: [Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Principality_of_Bulgaria/%22 "\\"Principality") was established as an independent principality inside the Ottoman Empire; [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/United_Principalities/%22 "\\"United") achieved full independence; and [Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Serbia/%22 "\\"History") and [Montenegro](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Montenegro/%22 "\\"Montenegro\\"") finally gained complete independence, but with smaller territories. In 1878, [Austria-Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Austria-Hungary/%22 "\\"Austria-Hungary\\"") unilaterally occupied the Ottoman provinces of [Bosnia-Herzegovina](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bosnia_Vilayet/%22 "\\"Bosnia") and [Novi Pazar](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sanjak_of_Novi_Pazar/%22 "\\"Sanjak").\\n

British Prime Minister [Benjamin Disraeli](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli/%22 "\\"Benjamin") advocated restoring the Ottoman territories on the Balkan Peninsula during the [Congress of Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin/%22 "\\"Congress"), and in return, Britain assumed the administration of [Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Cyprus/%22 "\\"Cyprus\\"") in 1878.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-154\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-154\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>140<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 228–254\"="">: 228–254 </span></sup>  Britain later sent troops to [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Egypt/%22 "\\"Egypt\\"") in 1882 to put down the [Urabi Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Urabi_Revolt/%22 "\\"Urabi") (Sultan [Abdul Hamid II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II/%22 "\\"Abdul") was too paranoid to mobilize his own army, fearing this would result in a coup d'état), effectively gaining control in both territories. Abdul Hamid II was so fearful of a coup that he did not allow his army to conduct war games, lest this serve as cover for a coup, but he did see the need for military mobilization. In 1883, a German military mission under General Baron [Colmar von der Goltz](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Colmar_Freiherr_von_der_Goltz/%22 "\\"Colmar") arrived to train the Ottoman Army, leading to the so-called \\"Goltz generation\\" of German-trained officers, who played a notable role in the politics of the empire's last years.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-155\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-155\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>141<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 24\"="">: 24 </span></sup> \\n

From 1894 to 1896, between 100,000 and 300,000 Armenians living throughout the empire were killed in what became known as the [Hamidian massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hamidian_massacres/%22 "\\"Hamidian").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-156\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-156\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>142<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;reference" nowrap\"=""><span title="\&quot;Page" location:="" 42\"="">: 42 </span></sup> \\n

In 1897 the population was 19 million, of whom 14 million (74%) were Muslim. An additional 20 million lived in provinces that remained under the sultan's nominal suzerainty but were entirely outside his actual power. One by one the Porte lost nominal authority. They included Egypt, Tunisia, Bulgaria, Cyprus, Bosnia-Herzegovina, and Lebanon.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-157\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-157\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>143<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

As the Ottoman Empire gradually shrank, 7–9 million Muslims from its former territories in the Caucasus, [Crimea](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Crimea/%22 "\\"Crimea\\""), Balkans, and the [Mediterranean](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mediterranean/%22 "\\"Mediterranean\\"") islands migrated to Anatolia and [Eastern Thrace](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Eastern_Thrace/%22 "\\"Eastern").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Karpat2004_158-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Karpat2004-158\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>144<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-159\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-159\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>145<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-160\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-160\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>146<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-161\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-161\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>147<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> After the Empire lost the [First Balkan War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/First_Balkan_War/%22 "\\"First") (1912–1913), it lost all its [Balkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Balkan_peninsula/%22 "\\"Balkan") territories except [East Thrace](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/East_Thrace/%22 "\\"East") (European Turkey). This resulted in around 400,000 Muslims fleeing with the retreating Ottoman armies (with many dying from [cholera](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Cholera/%22 "\\"Cholera\\"") brought by the soldiers), and 400,000 non-Muslims fled territory still under Ottoman rule.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-162\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-162\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>148<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> [Justin McCarthy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Justin_McCarthy_\(American_historian\)/%22 "\\"Justin") estimates that from 1821 to 1922, 5.5 million Muslims died in southeastern Europe, with the expulsion of 5 million.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-McCarthy1995_163-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-McCarthy1995-163\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>149<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Carmichael2012_164-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Carmichael2012-164\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>150<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Buturovic2010_165-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Buturovic2010-165\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>151<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

### Defeat and dissolution (1908–1922)

\\n

Main articles: [Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Dissolution") and [Ottoman Empire in World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Empire_in_World_War_I/%22 "\\"Ottoman")

\\n

#### Young Turk movement

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png/250px-Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png/%22)

Declaration of the [Young Turk Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution/%22 "\\"Young") by the leaders of the Ottoman [millets](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\)/%22 "\\"Millet") in 1908

\\n

The defeat and [dissolution of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Dissolution") (1908—1922) began with the [Second Constitutional Era](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era/%22 "\\"Second"), a moment of hope and promise established with the [Young Turk Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution/%22 "\\"Young"). It restored the [Constitution of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Constitution") and brought in [multi-party politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"List") with a [two-stage electoral system](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Elections_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Elections") ([electoral law](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_electoral_law/%22 "\\"Ottoman")) under the [Ottoman parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"General"). The constitution offered hope by freeing the empire's citizens to modernise the state's institutions, rejuvenate its strength, and enable it to hold its own against outside powers. Its guarantee of liberties promised to dissolve inter-communal tensions and transform the empire into a more harmonious place.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-166\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-166\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>152<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Instead, this period became the story of the twilight struggle of the Empire.\\n

Members of [Young Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Young_Turks/%22 "\\"Young") movement who had once gone underground now established their parties.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-167\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-167\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>153<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Among them \\"[Committee of Union and Progress](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress/%22 "\\"Committee")\\", and \\"[Freedom and Accord Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Freedom_and_Accord_Party/%22 "\\"Freedom")\\" were major parties. On the other end of the spectrum were ethnic parties, which included [Poale Zion](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Jewish_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party_in_Palestine_\(Poale_Zion\)/%22 "\\"Jewish"), [Al-Fatat](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Al-Fatat/%22 "\\"Al-Fatat\\""), and [Armenian national movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_national_movement/%22 "\\"Armenian") organised under [Armenian Revolutionary Federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation/%22 "\\"Armenian"). Profiting from the civil strife, Austria-Hungary officially annexed [Bosnia and Herzegovina](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina/%22 "\\"Bosnia") in 1908. The last of the [Ottoman censuses](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Census_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Census") was performed in [1914](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/1914_population_statistics_for_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"1914"). Despite [military reforms](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_military_reforms/%22 "\\"Ottoman") which reconstituted the [Ottoman Modern Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Modern_Army/%22 "\\"Ottoman"), the Empire lost its North African territories and the Dodecanese in the [Italo-Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War/%22 "\\"Italo-Turkish") (1911) and almost all of its European territories in the [Balkan Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Balkan_Wars/%22 "\\"Balkan") (1912–1913). The Empire faced continuous unrest in the years leading up to [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/World_War_I/%22 "\\"World"), including the [31 March Incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/31_March_Incident/%22 "\\"31") and two further coups in [1912](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/1912_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat/%22 "\\"1912") and [1913](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat/%22 "\\"1913").\\n

\\n

#### World War I

\\n

Main articles: [Ottoman entry into World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_entry_into_World_War_I/%22 "\\"Ottoman") and [Ottoman Empire in World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Empire_in_World_War_I/%22 "\\"Ottoman")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/M_113_5_amiral_Souchon_et_ses_officiers.jpg/250px-M_113_5_amiral_Souchon_et_ses_officiers.jpg/%22)

Admiral [Wilhelm Souchon](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wilhelm_Souchon/%22 "\\"Wilhelm"), who commanded the [Black Sea raid](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Black_Sea_raid/%22 "\\"Black") on 29 October 1914, and his officers in Ottoman naval uniforms

\\n

The Ottoman Empire entered [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/World_War_I/%22 "\\"World") on the side of the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Central_Powers/%22 "\\"Central") and was ultimately defeated.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-168\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-168\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>154<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman participation in the war began with the combined [German-Ottoman surprise attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Black_Sea_Raid/%22 "\\"Black") on the [Black Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Black_Sea/%22 "\\"Black") coast of the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Russian_Empire/%22 "\\"Russian") on 29 October 1914. Following the attack, the Russian Empire (2 November 1914)<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-oxfordreference-timeline_169-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-oxfordreference-timeline-169\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>155<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and its allies [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/French_Third_Republic/%22 "\\"French") (5 November 1914)<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-oxfordreference-timeline_169-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-oxfordreference-timeline-169\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>155<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/British_Empire/%22 "\\"British") (5 November 1914)<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-oxfordreference-timeline_169-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-oxfordreference-timeline-169\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>155<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> declared war on the Ottoman Empire. Also on 5 November 1914, the British government changed the status of the [Khedivate of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt/%22 "\\"Khedivate") and [Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Cyprus_Convention/%22 "\\"Cyprus"), which were [de jure](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/De_jure/%22 "\\"De") Ottoman territories prior to the war, to [British protectorates](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/British_protectorate/%22 "\\"British").\\n

The Ottomans successfully defended the [Dardanelles](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dardanelles/%22 "\\"Dardanelles\\"") strait during the [Gallipoli campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Gallipoli_campaign/%22 "\\"Gallipoli") (1915–1916) and achieved initial victories against British forces in the first two years of the [Mesopotamian campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mesopotamian_campaign/%22 "\\"Mesopotamian"), such as the [Siege of Kut](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Kut/%22 "\\"Siege") (1915–1916); but the [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Arab_Revolt/%22 "\\"Arab") (1916–1918) turned the tide against the Ottomans in the Middle East. In the [Caucasus campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caucasus_campaign/%22 "\\"Caucasus"), however, the Russian forces had the upper hand from the beginning, especially after the [Battle of Sarikamish](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Sarikamish/%22 "\\"Battle") (1914–1915). Russian forces advanced into northeastern [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anatolia/%22 "\\"Anatolia\\"") and controlled the major cities there until retreating from World War I with the [Treaty of Brest-Litovsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk/%22 "\\"Treaty") following the [Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Russian_Revolution/%22 "\\"Russian") in 1917.\\n

\\n

##### Genocides

\\n

Main articles: [Late Ottoman genocides](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Late_Ottoman_genocides/%22 "\\"Late"), [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_genocide/%22 "\\"Armenian"), [Greek genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Greek_genocide/%22 "\\"Greek"), and [Seyfo](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Seyfo/%22 "\\"Seyfo\\"")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Column_of_deportees_walking_through_Harput_vilayet_during_the_Armenian_genocide.jpg/250px-Column_of_deportees_walking_through_Harput_vilayet_during_the_Armenian_genocide.jpg/%22)

The [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_genocide/%22 "\\"Armenian") was the result of the Ottoman government's [deportation](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Temporary_Law_of_Deportation/%22 "\\"Temporary") and [ethnic cleansing](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing/%22 "\\"Ethnic") policies regarding its [Armenian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenians_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Armenians") citizens after the [Battle of Sarikamish](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Battle_of_Sarikamish/%22 "\\"Battle") (1914–1915) and the collapse of the [Caucasus Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caucasus_campaign/%22 "\\"Caucasus") against the [Imperial Russian Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Army/%22 "\\"Imperial") and [Armenian volunteer units](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_volunteer_units/%22 "\\"Armenian") during [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/World_War_I/%22 "\\"World"). An estimated 600,000<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-britannica-ag_170-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-britannica-ag-170\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>156<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> to more than 1 million,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-britannica-ag_170-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-britannica-ag-170\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>156<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> or up to 1.5 million<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-171\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-171\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>157<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-172\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-172\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>158<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-173\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-173\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>159<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> people were killed.

\\n

In 1915 the Ottoman government and Kurdish tribes in the region started the extermination of its ethnic Armenian population, resulting in the deaths of up to 1.5 million Armenians in the [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_genocide/%22 "\\"Armenian").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-174\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-174\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>160<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-175\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-175\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>161<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-176\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-176\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>162<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The genocide was carried out during and after World War I and implemented in two phases: the wholesale killing of the able-bodied male population through massacre and subjection of army conscripts to forced labour, followed by the deportation of women, children, the elderly and infirm on [death marches](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Death_march/%22 "\\"Death") leading to the [Syrian desert](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Syrian_desert/%22 "\\"Syrian"). Driven forward by military escorts, the deportees were deprived of food and water and subjected to periodic robbery, [rape](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rape_during_the_Armenian_Genocide/%22 "\\"Rape"), and systematic massacre.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-177\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-177\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>163<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-178\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-178\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>164<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Large-scale massacres were also committed against the Empire's [Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Greek_genocide/%22 "\\"Greek") and [Assyrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Assyrian_genocide/%22 "\\"Assyrian") minorities as part of the same campaign of ethnic cleansing.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-179\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-179\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>165<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

##### Arab Revolt

\\n

Main articles: [Middle Eastern theatre of World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Middle_Eastern_theatre_of_World_War_I/%22 "\\"Middle") and [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Arab_Revolt/%22 "\\"Arab")

\\n

The [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Arab_Revolt/%22 "\\"Arab") began in 1916 with British support. It turned the tide against the Ottomans on the Middle Eastern front, where they seemed to have the upper hand during the first two years of the war. On the basis of the [McMahon–Hussein Correspondence](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/McMahon%E2%80%93Hussein_Correspondence/%22 "\\"McMahon–Hussein"), an agreement between the British government and [Hussein bin Ali, Sharif of Mecca](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_Sharif_of_Mecca/%22 "\\"Hussein"), the revolt was officially initiated at Mecca on 10 June 1916.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-181\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-181\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>o<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Arab nationalist goal was to create a single unified and independent [Arab state](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Arab_state/%22 "\\"Arab") stretching from [Aleppo](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Aleppo/%22 "\\"Aleppo\\""), Syria, to [Aden](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Aden/%22 "\\"Aden\\""), Yemen, which the British promised to recognise.\\n

The [Sharifian Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sharifian_Army/%22 "\\"Sharifian"), led by Hussein and the [Hashemites](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hashemites/%22 "\\"Hashemites\\""), with military backing from the British [Egyptian Expeditionary Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Egyptian_Expeditionary_Force/%22 "\\"Egyptian"), successfully fought and expelled the Ottoman military presence from much of the [Hejaz](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hejaz/%22 "\\"Hejaz\\"") and [Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Transjordan_\(region\)/%22 "\\"Transjordan"). The rebellion eventually took [Damascus](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Damascus/%22 "\\"Damascus\\"") and set up a short-lived monarchy led by [Faisal](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Faisal_I_of_Iraq/%22 "\\"Faisal"), a son of Hussein.\\n

Following the terms of the 1916 [Sykes–Picot Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement/%22 "\\"Sykes–Picot"), the British and French later partitioned the Middle East into [mandate territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate/%22 "\\"League"). There was no unified Arab state, much to Arab nationalists' anger. Palestine, Iraq, Lebanon and Syria became British and French mandates.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-182\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-182\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>167<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

##### Treaty of Sèvres and Turkish War of Independence

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sultanvahideddin.jpg/250px-Sultanvahideddin.jpg/%22)

[Mehmed VI](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_VI/%22 "\\"Mehmed"), the last Sultan of the Ottoman Empire, leaving the country after the abolition of the Ottoman sultanate, 17 November 1922

\\n

Defeated in World War I, the Ottoman Empire signed the [Armistice of Mudros](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armistice_of_Mudros/%22 "\\"Armistice") on 30 October 1918. [Istanbul was occupied](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Occupation_of_Istanbul/%22 "\\"Occupation") by combined British, French, Italian, and Greek forces. In May 1919, Greece also [took control of the area around Smyrna](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Occupation_of_Smyrna/%22 "\\"Occupation") (now İzmir).\\n

The [partition of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Partition") was finalized under the terms of the 1920 [Treaty of Sèvres](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres/%22 "\\"Treaty"). This treaty, as designed in the [Conference of London](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Conference_of_London_\(1920\)/%22 "\\"Conference"), allowed the Sultan to retain his position and title. Anatolia's status was problematic given the occupied forces.\\n

A nationalist opposition arose in the [Turkish national movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkish_national_movement/%22 "\\"Turkish"). It won the [Turkish War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence/%22 "\\"Turkish") (1919–1923) under the leadership of [Mustafa Kemal](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk/%22 "\\"Mustafa") (later given the surname \\"Atatürk\\"). The sultanate was abolished on 1 November 1922, and the last sultan, [Mehmed VI](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_VI/%22 "\\"Mehmed") (reigned 1918–1922), left the country on 17 November 1922. The [Republic of Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkey/%22 "\\"Turkey\\"") was [established](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Turkey#Republic_of_Turkey\%22 "\\"History") in its place on 29 October 1923, in the new capital city of [Ankara](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ankara/%22 "\\"Ankara\\""). The [caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate/%22 "\\"Ottoman") was abolished on 3 March 1924.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Ozoglu_183-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Ozoglu-183\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>168<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-184\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-184\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>169<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

## Historiographical debate on the Ottoman state

See also: [Ghaza thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ghaza_thesis/%22 "\\"Ghaza")

| \\n [Medieval Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Middle_Ages/%22 "\\"Middle") - [Medieval Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Medieval_Anatolia/%22 "\\"Medieval") \\n \| [Eastern Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire/%22 "\\"Eastern") \| (330–1453; 1204-1261 in exile as [Empire of Nicaea](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Empire_of_Nicaea/%22 "\\"Empire")) \| \| --- \| --- \| \| [Rashidun Caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate/%22 "\\"Rashidun") \| (637–656) \| \| [Great Seljuk State](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Seljuk_Empire/%22 "\\"Seljuk") \| (1037–1194) \| \| [Danishmends](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Danishmends/%22 "\\"Danishmends\\"") \| (1071–1178) \| \| [Sultanate of Rum](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum/%22 "\\"Sultanate") \| (1077–1307) \| \| [Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_Kingdom_of_Cilicia/%22 "\\"Armenian") \| (1078–1375) \| \| [Anatolian beyliks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anatolian_beyliks/%22 "\\"Anatolian") \| (1081–1423) \| \| [County of Edessa](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/County_of_Edessa/%22 "\\"County") \| (1098–1150) \| \| [Artuqids](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Artuqids/%22 "\\"Artuqids\\"") \| (1101–1409) \| \| [Empire of Trebizond](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Empire_of_Trebizond/%22 "\\"Empire") \| (1204–1461) \| \| [Latin Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Latin_Empire/%22 "\\"Latin") \| (1204–1261) \| \| [Karamanids](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Karamanids/%22 "\\"Karamanids\\"") \| (1250–1487) \| \| [Ilkhanate](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ilkhanate/%22 "\\"Ilkhanate\\"") \| (1256–1335) \| \| [Kara Koyunlu](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kara_Koyunlu/%22 "\\"Kara") \| (1375–1468) \| \| [Ak Koyunlu](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Aq_Qoyunlu/%22 "\\"Aq") \| (1378–1501) \| |
| \\n Ottoman Era - [Periods of Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"History") \\n \| [Rise](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rise_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Rise") \| (1299–1453) \| \| --- \| --- \| \| [Classical Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Classical_Age_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Classical") \| (1453–1566) \| \| [Transformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Transformation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Transformation") \| (1566–1703) \| \| [Old Regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Old_Regime/%22 "\\"Ottoman") \| (1703–1789) \| \| [Decline and modernization](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Decline_and_modernization_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_\(1828%E2%80%931908\)/%22 "\\"Decline") \| (1789–1908) \| \| [Defeat and dissolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Defeat_and_dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_\(1908%E2%80%931922\)/%22 "\\"Defeat") \| (1908–1922) \| |
| \\n [Republic of Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkey/%22 "\\"Turkey\\"") - [Periods of Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"History") \\n \| [War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence/%22 "\\"Turkish") \| (1919–1922) \| \| --- \| --- \| \| [Provisional government](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Government_of_the_Grand_National_Assembly/%22 "\\"Government") \| (1920–1923) \| \| [One-party period](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/One-party_period_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"One-party") \| (1923–1930) (1930–1945) \| \| [Multi-party period](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Multi-party_period_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Multi-party") \| (1945–present) \| |
| \\n By topic \\n - [Turkic migration](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkic_migration/%22 "\\"Turkic")\\n 	- [Oghuz Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Oghuz_Turks/%22 "\\"Oghuz") \\n- [Turkification](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkification/%22 "\\"Turkification\\"") \\n- [Ancient peoples of Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/List_of_ancient_peoples_of_Anatolia/%22 "\\"List") \\n- [History of Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Anatolia/%22 "\\"History") \\n- [History of Thrace](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Thrace/%22 "\\"History") \\n- [Religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Religion_in_Turkey/%22 "\\"Religion")\\n 	- [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Islam_in_Turkey#History\%22 "\\"Islam") 	\\n- [Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Christianity_in_Turkey/%22 "\\"History") 	\\n- [Judaism](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Turkey/%22 "\\"History") \\n- [Economic history](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Economic_history_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Economic") \\n- [Military history](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Military_history_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Military") \\n- [Diplomatic history](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Diplomatic_history_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Diplomatic") \\n- [Constitutional history](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Constitutional_history_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Constitutional") \\n- [Cultural history](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Culture_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Culture") \\n- [Genetic history](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Genetic_history_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Genetic") \\n- [LGBT history](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/LGBT_history_in_Turkey/%22 "\\"LGBT") \\n |

| \\n ![\"flag\"](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/20px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png/%22)[Turkey portal](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Portal:Turkey/%22 "\\"Portal:Turkey\\"") |
| - [v](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Template:History_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Template:History") - [t](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Template") - [e](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:History_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Special:EditPage/Template:History") |

\\n

Several historians, such as British historian [Edward Gibbon](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Edward_Gibbon/%22 "\\"Edward") and the Greek historian [Dimitri Kitsikis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dimitri_Kitsikis/%22 "\\"Dimitri"), have argued that after the fall of Constantinople, the Ottoman state took over the machinery of the Byzantine (Roman) state and that the Ottoman Empire was in essence a continuation of the Byzantine Empire under a [Turkish](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkish_people/%22 "\\"Turkish") [Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muslims/%22 "\\"Muslims\\"") guise.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-185\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-185\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>170<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The American historian [Speros Vryonis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Speros_Vryonis/%22 "\\"Speros") writes that the Ottoman state centered on \\"a Byzantine-Balkan base with a veneer of the Turkish language and the Islamic religion\\".<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Stone,_pp._86-100_186-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Stone,_pp._86-100-186\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>171<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Kitsikis and the American historian [Heath Lowry](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Heath_Lowry/%22 "\\"Heath") posit that the early Ottoman state was a predatory confederacy open to both Byzantine Christians and Turkish Muslims whose primary goal was attaining booty and slaves, rather than spreading Islam, and that Islam only later became the empire's primary characteristic.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-187\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-187\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>172<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-188\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-188\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>173<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-189\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-189\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>174<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Other historians have followed the lead of the Austrian historian [Paul Wittek](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Paul_Wittek/%22 "\\"Paul"), who emphasizes the early Ottoman state's Islamic character, seeing it as a \\"[jihad](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Jihad/%22 "\\"Jihad\\"") state\\" dedicated to expanding the [Muslim world](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muslim_world/%22 "\\"Muslim").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Stone,_pp._86-100_186-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Stone,_pp._86-100-186\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>171<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Many historians led in 1937 by the Turkish historian [Mehmet Fuat Köprülü](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmet_Fuat_K%C3%B6pr%C3%BCl%C3%BC/%22 "\\"Mehmet") championed the [Ghaza thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ghaza_thesis/%22 "\\"Ghaza"), according to which the early Ottoman state was a continuation of the way of life of the nomadic [Turkic tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkic_peoples/%22 "\\"Turkic") who had come from East Asia to Anatolia via Central Asia and the Middle East on a much larger scale. They argued that the most important cultural influences on the Ottoman state came from [Persia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Iran/%22 "\\"Iran\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-190\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-190\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>175<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The British historian [Norman Stone](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Norman_Stone/%22 "\\"Norman") suggests many continuities between the Byzantine and Ottoman empires, such as that the *zeugarion* tax of Byzantium became the Ottoman *[Resm-i çift](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Resm-i_%C3%A7ift/%22 "\\"Resm-i")* tax, that the *[pronoia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Pronoia/%22 "\\"Pronoia\\"")* land-holding system that linked the amount of land one owned with one's ability to raise cavalry became the Ottoman *[timar](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Timar/%22 "\\"Timar\\"")* system, and that the Ottoman land measurement the *[dönüm](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/D%C3%B6n%C3%BCm/%22 "\\"Dönüm\\"")* was the same as the Byzantine *[stremma](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Stremma/%22 "\\"Stremma\\"")*. Stone also argues that although Sunni Islam was the state religion, the Ottoman state supported and controlled the [Eastern Orthodox Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church/%22 "\\"Eastern"), which in return for accepting that control became the Ottoman Empire's largest land-holder. Despite the similarities, Stone argues that a crucial difference is that the land grants under the *timar* system were not hereditary at first. Even after they became inheritable, land ownership in the Ottoman Empire remained highly insecure, and the sultan revoked land grants whenever he wished. Stone argued this insecurity in land tenure strongly discouraged *[Timariots](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Timariot/%22 "\\"Timariot\\"")* from seeking long-term development of their land, and instead led them to adopt a strategy of short-term exploitation, which had deleterious effects on the Ottoman economy.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-191\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-191\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>176<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

## Government

\\n

Main article: [State organisation of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/State_organisation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"State")

\\n

[![\"\"](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg/250px-Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg/%22)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/File:Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg/%22)

[![\"\"](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace%2C_Istanbul_cropped.jpg/250px-Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace%2C_Istanbul_cropped.jpg/%22)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/File:Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace,_Istanbul_cropped.jpg/%22)

[Topkapı Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace/%22 "\\"Topkapı") and [Dolmabahçe Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace/%22 "\\"Dolmabahçe") were the primary residences of the [Ottoman sultans](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"List") in [Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Istanbul/%22 "\\"Istanbul\\"") between 1465 and 1856<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-nytimes_192-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-nytimes-192\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>177<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and 1856 to 1922,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-dolmabahcepalace_193-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-dolmabahcepalace-193\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>178<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> respectively.

\\n

Before the reforms of the 19th and 20th centuries, the [state organisation of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/State_organisation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"State") was a system with two main dimensions, the military administration, and the civil administration. The Sultan was in the highest position in the system. The civil system was based on local administrative units based on the region's characteristics. The state had control over the clergy. Certain pre-Islamic Turkish traditions that had survived the adoption of administrative and legal practices from Islamic [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Iran/%22 "\\"Iran\\"") remained important in Ottoman administrative circles.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198038_194-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198038-194\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>179<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> According to Ottoman understanding, the state's primary responsibility was to defend and extend the land of the Muslims and to ensure security and harmony within its borders in the overarching context of [orthodox](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sunni/%22 "\\"Sunni\\"") Islamic practice and dynastic sovereignty.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Kapucu-2008_195-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Kapucu-2008-195\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>180<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The Ottoman Empire, or as a dynastic institution, the House of Osman, was unprecedented and unequaled in the Islamic world for its size and duration.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-196\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-196\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>181<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In Europe, only the [House of Habsburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/House_of_Habsburg/%22 "\\"House") had a similarly unbroken line of sovereigns (kings/emperors) from the same family who ruled for so long, and during the same period, between the late 13th and early 20th centuries. The Ottoman dynasty was Turkish in origin. On eleven occasions, the sultan was deposed (replaced by another sultan of the Ottoman dynasty, who were either the former sultan's brother, son or nephew) because he was perceived by his enemies as a threat to the state. There were only two attempts in Ottoman history to unseat the ruling Ottoman dynasty, both failures, which suggests a political system that for an extended period was able to manage its revolutions without unnecessary instability.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Kapucu-2008_195-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Kapucu-2008-195\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>180<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> As such, the last Ottoman sultan Mehmed VI (r. 1918–1922) was a [direct patrilineal (male-line) descendant](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"List") of the first Ottoman sultan [Osman I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Osman_I/%22 "\\"Osman") (d. 1323/4), which was unparalleled in both Europe (e.g., the male line of the House of Habsburg became extinct in 1740) and in the Islamic world.
