The primary purpose of the [Imperial Harem](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Imperial_Harem/%22 "\\"Imperial") was to ensure the birth of male heirs to the Ottoman throne and secure the continuation of the direct patrilineal (male-line) power of the Ottoman sultans in the future generations.\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/250px-Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/%22)

Ambassadors at the Topkapı Palace

\\n

The highest position in Islam, [caliph](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caliphate/%22 "\\"Caliphate\\""), was claimed by the sultans starting with [Selim I](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Selim_I/%22 "\\"Selim"),<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Lambton-1995_25-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Lambton-1995-25\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>18<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> which was established as the Ottoman Caliphate. The Ottoman sultan, *[pâdişâh](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Padishah/%22 "\\"Padishah\\"")* or \\"lord of kings\\", served as the Empire's sole regent and was considered to be the embodiment of its government, though he did not always exercise complete control. The Imperial Harem was one of the most important powers of the Ottoman court. It was ruled by the [valide sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Valide_sultan/%22 "\\"Valide"). On occasion, the valide sultan became involved in state politics. For a time, the women of the Harem effectively controlled the state in what was termed the \\"[Sultanate of Women](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sultanate_of_the_women/%22 "\\"Sultanate")\\". New sultans were always chosen from the sons of the previous sultan.<sup class="\&quot;noprint" inline-template\"="" style="\&quot;white-space:nowrap;\&quot;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement\%22" title="\&quot;Wikipedia:Accuracy" dispute\"=""><span title="\&quot;this" is="" demonstrably="" not="" true,="" just="" look="" at="" any="" list="" of="" sultans="" (september="" 2016)\"="">dubious</span></a> – <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Talk:Ottoman_Empire#Dubious\%22" title="\&quot;Talk:Ottoman" empire\"="">discuss</a></i>]</sup> The strong educational system of the [palace school](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Palace_school/%22 "\\"Palace") was geared towards eliminating the unfit potential heirs and establishing support among the ruling elite for a successor. The palace schools, which also educated the future administrators of the state, were not a single track. First, the [Madrasa](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Madrasa/%22 "\\"Madrasa\\"") (*Medrese*) was designated for the Muslims, and educated scholars and state officials according to Islamic tradition. The financial burden of the Medrese was supported by *[vakif](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Waqf/%22 "\\"Waqf\\"")*s, allowing children of poor families to move to higher social levels and income.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-197\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-197\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>182<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The second track was a free [boarding school](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Boarding_school/%22 "\\"Boarding") for the Christians, the *[Enderûn](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ender%C3%BBn/%22 "\\"Enderûn\\"")*,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-198\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-198\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>183<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> which recruited 3,000 students annually from Christian boys between eight and twenty years old from one in forty families among the communities settled in [Rumelia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rumelia/%22 "\\"Rumelia\\"") or the Balkans, a process known as [Devshirme](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Devshirme_in_the_Ottoman_Palace_School/%22 "\\"Devshirme") (*Devşirme*).<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-199\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-199\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>184<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Devshirme falls within modern definitions of [genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Genocide/%22 "\\"Genocide\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-a852_200-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-a852-200\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>185<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-v450_201-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-v450-201\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>186<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Though the sultan was the supreme monarch, the sultan's political and executive authority was delegated. The politics of the state had a number of advisors and ministers gathered around a council known as [Divan](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Divan/%22 "\\"Divan\\""). The Divan, in the years when the Ottoman state was still a *[Beylik](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bey/%22 "\\"Bey\\"")*, was composed of the elders of the tribe. Its composition was later modified to include military officers and local elites (such as religious and political advisors). Later still, beginning in 1320, a Grand Vizier was appointed to assume certain of the sultan's responsibilities. The Grand Vizier had considerable independence from the sultan with almost unlimited powers of appointment, dismissal, and supervision. Beginning with the late 16th century, sultans withdrew from politics and the Grand Vizier became the *de facto* head of state.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Black-2001_202-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Black-2001-202\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>187<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg/250px-Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg/%22)

[Yusuf Ziya Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Yusuf_Ziya_Pasha/%22 "\\"Yusuf"), Ottoman ambassador to the United States, in [Washington DC](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Washington,_D.C./%22 "\\"Washington,"), 1913

\\n

Throughout Ottoman history, there were many instances in which local governors acted independently, and even in opposition to the ruler. After the Young Turk Revolution of 1908, the Ottoman state became a constitutional monarchy. The sultan no longer had executive powers. A parliament was formed, with representatives chosen from the provinces. The representatives formed the [Imperial Government of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Imperial_Government_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Imperial").\\n

This eclectic administration was apparent even in the diplomatic correspondence of the Empire, which was initially undertaken in the [Greek language](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Greek_language/%22 "\\"Greek") to the west.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-203\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-203\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>188<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The [Tughra](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tughra/%22 "\\"Tughra\\"") were calligraphic monograms, or signatures, of the Ottoman Sultans, of which there were 35. Carved on the Sultan's seal, they bore the names of the Sultan and his father. The statement and prayer, \\"ever victorious\\", was also present in most. The earliest belonged to Orhan Gazi. The ornately stylized *Tughra* spawned a branch of Ottoman-Turkish [calligraphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Calligraphy/%22 "\\"Calligraphy\\"").\\n

\\n

### Law

\\n

Main article: [Law of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Law_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Law")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Zibik.jpg/250px-Zibik.jpg/%22)

An unhappy wife complaining to the [Qadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Qadi/%22 "\\"Qadi\\"") about her husband's [impotence](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Erectile_dysfunction/%22 "\\"Erectile"), as depicted in an Ottoman miniature. [Divorce](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Divorce/%22 "\\"Divorce\\"") is [allowed](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Religion_and_divorce#Islam\%22 "\\"Religion") in [Islamic law](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sharia/%22 "\\"Sharia\\"") and [can be initiated by either the husband or the wife](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Divorce_in_Islam/%22 "\\"Divorce").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-204\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-204\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>189<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>

\\n

The Ottoman legal system accepted the [religious law](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Religious_law/%22 "\\"Religious") over its subjects. At the same time the *[Qanun](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Qanun_\(law\)/%22 "\\"Qanun")* (or *Kanun*), dynastic law, co-existed with religious law or [Sharia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sharia/%22 "\\"Sharia\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-otmkanun_205-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-otmkanun-205\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>190<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-206\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-206\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>191<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman Empire was always organized around a system of local [jurisprudence](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Jurisprudence/%22 "\\"Jurisprudence\\""). Legal administration in the Ottoman Empire was part of a larger scheme of balancing central and local authority.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Benton-2001-207\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>192<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Ottoman power revolved crucially around the administration of the rights to land, which gave a space for the local authority to develop the needs of the local [millet](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\)/%22 "\\"Millet").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Benton-2001-207\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>192<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The jurisdictional complexity of the Ottoman Empire was aimed to permit the integration of culturally and religiously different groups.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Benton-2001-207\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>192<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman system had three court systems: one for Muslims, one for non-Muslims, involving appointed Jews and Christians ruling over their respective religious communities, and the \\"trade court\\". The entire system was regulated from above by means of the administrative *Qanun*, i.e., laws, a system based upon the Turkic *[Yassa](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Yassa/%22 "\\"Yassa\\"")* and *[Töre](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/w/index.php?title=T%C3%B6re_\(law\)&action=edit&redlink=1\%22 "\\"Töre")*, which were developed in the pre-Islamic era.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-208\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-208\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>193<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-209\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-209\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>194<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

These court categories were not, however, wholly exclusive; for instance, the Islamic courts, which were the Empire's primary courts, could also be used to settle a trade conflict or disputes between litigants of differing religions, and Jews and Christians often went to them to obtain a more forceful ruling on an issue. The Ottoman state tended not to interfere with non-Muslim religious law systems, despite legally having a voice to do so through local governors. The Islamic *Sharia* law system had been developed from a combination of the [Qur'an](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Qur%27an/%22 "\\"Qur'an\\""); the [Hadīth](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hadith/%22 "\\"Hadith\\""), or words of [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muhammad_in_Islam/%22 "\\"Muhammad"); *[ijmā'](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ijma/%22 "\\"Ijma\\"")*, or consensus of the members of the [Muslim community](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ummah/%22 "\\"Ummah\\""); [qiyas](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Qiyas/%22 "\\"Qiyas\\""), a system of analogical reasoning from earlier precedents; and local customs. Both systems were taught at the Empire's law schools, which were in [Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Istanbul/%22 "\\"Istanbul\\"") and [Bursa](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bursa/%22 "\\"Bursa\\"").\\n

 
\\nThe Ottoman Islamic legal system was set up differently from traditional European courts. Presiding over Islamic courts was a *Qadi*, or judge. Since the closing of the *[ijtihad](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ijtihad/%22 "\\"Ijtihad\\"")*, or 'Gate of Interpretation', *Qadi*s throughout the Ottoman Empire focused less on legal precedent, and more with local customs and traditions in the areas that they administered.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-3\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Benton-2001-207\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>192<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> However, the Ottoman court system lacked an appellate structure, leading to jurisdictional case strategies where plaintiffs could take their disputes from one court system to another until they achieved a ruling that was in their favour.\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png/290px-1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png/%22)

An Ottoman trial, 1877

\\n

In the late 19th century, the Ottoman legal system saw substantial reform. This process of legal modernisation began with the [Edict of Gülhane](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Edict_of_G%C3%BClhane/%22 "\\"Edict") of 1839.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-review-niza_210-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-review-niza-210\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>195<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> These reforms included the \\"fair and public trial\[s\] of all accused regardless of religion\\", the creation of a system of \\"separate competences, religious and civil\\", and the validation of testimony on non-Muslims.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-int-handbook_211-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-int-handbook-211\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>196<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Specific land codes (1858), civil codes (1869–1876), and a code of civil procedure also were enacted.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-int-handbook_211-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-int-handbook-211\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>196<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

These reforms were based heavily on French models, as indicated by the adoption of a three-tiered court system. Referred to as [Nizamiye](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/w/index.php?title=Nizamiye&action=edit&redlink=1\%22 "\\"Nizamiye"), this system was extended to the local magistrate level with the final promulgation of the [Mecelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mecelle/%22 "\\"Mecelle\\""), a civil code that regulated marriage, divorce, alimony, will, and other matters of personal status.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-int-handbook_211-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-int-handbook-211\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>196<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In an attempt to clarify the division of judicial competences, an administrative council laid down that religious matters were to be handled by religious courts, and statute matters were to be handled by the Nizamiye courts.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-int-handbook_211-3\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-int-handbook-211\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>196<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

### Military

\\n

Main article: [Military of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Military_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Military")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/J%C3%B3zef_Brandt_-_Fight_for_a_Turkish_Standard_-_MNK_II-a-1318_-_National_Museum_Krak%C3%B3w.jpg/250px-J%C3%B3zef_Brandt_-_Fight_for_a_Turkish_Standard_-_MNK_II-a-1318_-_National_Museum_Krak%C3%B3w.jpg/%22)

Ottoman [sipahis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sipahi/%22 "\\"Sipahi\\"") in battle, holding the crescent banner, by [Józef Brandt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Brandt/%22 "\\"Józef")

\\n

The first military unit of the Ottoman State was an army that was organized by Osman I from the tribesmen inhabiting the hills of western Anatolia in the late 13th century. The military system became an intricate organization with the advance of the Empire. The Ottoman military was a complex system of recruiting and fief-holding. The main corps of the [Ottoman Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Army/%22 "\\"Ottoman") included Janissary, [Sipahi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sipahi/%22 "\\"Sipahi\\""), [Akıncı](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Akinji/%22 "\\"Akinji\\"") and [Mehterân](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_military_band/%22 "\\"Ottoman"). The Ottoman army was once among the most advanced fighting forces in the world, being one of the first to use muskets and cannons. The Ottoman Turks began using *[falconets](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Falconet_\(cannon\)/%22 "\\"Falconet")*, which were short but wide cannons, during the [Siege of Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Siege_of_Constantinople_\(1422\)/%22 "\\"Siege"). The Ottoman cavalry depended on high speed and mobility rather than heavy armor, using bows and short swords on fast [Turkoman](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkoman_horse/%22 "\\"Turkoman") and [Arabian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Arabian_horse/%22 "\\"Arabian") horses (progenitors of the [Thoroughbred](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Thoroughbred#Foundation_stallions\%22 "\\"Thoroughbred\\"") racing horse),<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-212\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-212\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>197<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-213\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-213\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>198<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and often applied tactics similar to those of the [Mongol Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mongol_Empire/%22 "\\"Mongol"), such as pretending to retreat while surrounding the enemy forces inside a crescent-shaped formation and then making the real attack. The Ottoman army continued to be an effective fighting force throughout the seventeenth and early eighteenth centuries,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-214\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-214\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>199<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-215\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-215\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>200<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> falling behind the empire's European rivals only during a long period of peace from 1740 to 1768.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-AksanOW_78-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-AksanOW-78\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>64<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/The_Ertugrul_Cavalry_Regiment_crossing_the_Galata_Bridge.jpg/250px-The_Ertugrul_Cavalry_Regiment_crossing_the_Galata_Bridge.jpg/%22)

Modernised [Ertugrul Cavalry Regiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Asakir-i_Mansure-i_Muhammediye/%22 "\\"Asakir-i") crossing the [Galata Bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Galata_Bridge/%22 "\\"Galata") in 1901

\\n

The modernization of the Ottoman Empire in the 19th century started with the military. In 1826 Sultan Mahmud II abolished the Janissary corps and established the modern Ottoman army. He named them as the [Nizam-ı Cedid](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Nizam-%C4%B1_Cedid/%22 "\\"Nizam-ı") (New Order). The Ottoman army was also the first institution to hire foreign experts and send its officers for training in western European countries. Consequently, the Young Turks movement began when these relatively young and newly trained men returned with their education.\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/OttomanNavy.jpg/250px-OttomanNavy.jpg/%22)

The [Ottoman fleet](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Navy/%22 "\\"Ottoman") in the [Bosphorous](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bosporus/%22 "\\"Bosporus\\"") near [Ortaköy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ortak%C3%B6y/%22 "\\"Ortaköy\\"")

\\n

The [Ottoman Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Navy/%22 "\\"Ottoman") vastly contributed to the expansion of the Empire's territories on the European continent. It initiated the conquest of North Africa, with the addition of [Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Algeria/%22 "\\"Algeria\\"") and Egypt to the Ottoman Empire in 1517. Starting with the loss of Greece in 1821 and Algeria in 1830, Ottoman naval power and control over the Empire's distant overseas territories began to decline. Sultan [Abdülaziz](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abd%C3%BClaziz/%22 "\\"Abdülaziz\\"") (reigned 1861–1876) attempted to reestablish a strong Ottoman navy, building the largest fleet after those of Britain and France. The shipyard at Barrow, England, built its first [submarine](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Submarine/%22 "\\"Submarine\\"") in 1886 for the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-first_submarine_at_shipyard_216-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-first_submarine_at_shipyard-216\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>201<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

However, the collapsing Ottoman economy could not sustain the fleet's strength for long. Sultan [Abdülhamid II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abd%C3%BClhamid_II/%22 "\\"Abdülhamid") distrusted the admirals who sided with the reformist [Midhat Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Midhat_Pasha/%22 "\\"Midhat") and claimed that the large and expensive fleet was of no use against the Russians during the Russo-Turkish War. He locked most of the fleet inside the [Golden Horn](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Golden_Horn/%22 "\\"Golden"), where the ships decayed for the next 30 years. Following the Young Turk Revolution in 1908, the Committee of Union and Progress sought to develop a strong Ottoman naval force. The *Ottoman Navy Foundation* was established in 1910 to buy new ships through public donations.\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg/250px-Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg/%22)

[Ottoman pilots](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Aviation_Squadrons/%22 "\\"Ottoman") in early 1912

\\n

The establishment of [Ottoman military aviation](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Air_Force/%22 "\\"Ottoman") dates back to between June 1909 and July 1911.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-217\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-217\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>202<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-218\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-218\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>203<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman Empire started preparing its first pilots and planes, and with the founding of the Aviation School (*Tayyare Mektebi*) in [Yeşilköy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ye%C5%9Filk%C3%B6y/%22 "\\"Yeşilköy\\"") on 3 July 1912, the Empire began to tutor its own flight officers. The founding of the Aviation School quickened advancement in the military aviation program, increased the number of enlisted persons within it, and gave the new pilots an active role in the Ottoman Army and Navy. In May 1913, the world's first specialized Reconnaissance Training Program was started by the Aviation School, and the first separate reconnaissance division was established.<sup class="\&quot;noprint" inline-template="" template-fact\"="" style="\&quot;white-space:nowrap;\&quot;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed/%22" title="\&quot;Wikipedia:Citation" needed\"=""><span title="\&quot;This" claim="" needs="" references="" to="" reliable="" sources.="" (june="" 2011)\"="">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In June 1914 a new military academy, the Naval Aviation School (*Bahriye Tayyare Mektebi*) was founded. With the outbreak of World War I, the modernization process stopped abruptly. The [Ottoman Aviation Squadrons](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Aviation_Squadrons/%22 "\\"Ottoman") fought on many fronts during World War I, from [Galicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Galicia_\(Central_Europe\)/%22 "\\"Galicia") in the west to the Caucasus in the east and [Yemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Yemen/%22 "\\"Yemen\\"") in the south.\\n

\\n

## Administrative divisions

\\n

Main article: [Administrative divisions of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Administrative")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Ottoman_Empire_Administrative_Divisions.png/220px-Ottoman_Empire_Administrative_Divisions.png/%22)

Administrative divisions of the Ottoman Empire in 1899 (year 1317 Hijri)

\\n

The Ottoman Empire was first subdivided into provinces, in the sense of fixed territorial units with governors appointed by the sultan, in the late 14th century.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Imber_219-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Imber-219\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>204<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The [Eyalet](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Eyalet/%22 "\\"Eyalet\\"") (also *Pashalik* or *Beylerbeylik*) was the territory of office of a [Beylerbey](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Beylerbey/%22 "\\"Beylerbey\\"") (\\"lord of lords\\" or governor), and was further subdivided into [Sanjaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sanjak/%22 "\\"Sanjak\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-220\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-220\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>205<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The [Vilayets](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Vilayets/%22 "\\"Vilayets\\"") were introduced with the promulgation of the \\"Vilayet Law\\" (*Teskil-i Vilayet Nizamnamesi*)<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-221\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-221\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>206<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> in 1864, as part of the Tanzimat reforms.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-trt_222-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-trt-222\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>207<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Unlike the previous eyalet system, the 1864 law established a hierarchy of administrative units: the vilayet, [liva](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Liva_\(sanjak\)/%22 "\\"Liva")/[sanjak](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sanjak/%22 "\\"Sanjak\\"")/[mutasarrifate](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mutasarrifate/%22 "\\"Mutasarrifate\\""), [kaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Kaza/%22 "\\"Kaza\\"") and [village council](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Town_council/%22 "\\"Town"), to which the 1871 Vilayet Law added the [nahiye](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Nahiye/%22 "\\"Nahiye\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-jpn_223-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-jpn-223\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>208<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

## Economy

\\n

Main article: [Economic history of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Economic")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ayd%C4%B1nArchaeologicalMuseum_%28117%29.JPG/250px-Ayd%C4%B1nArchaeologicalMuseum_%28117%29.JPG/%22)

Coins of the Sultanate of Rûm and the Ottoman Empire at [Aydın Archaeological Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ayd%C4%B1n_Archaeological_Museum/%22 "\\"Aydın")

\\n

Ottoman government deliberately pursued a policy for the development of Bursa, Edirne, and Istanbul, successive Ottoman capitals, into major commercial and industrial centers, considering that merchants and artisans were indispensable in creating a new metropolis.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Inalcik1970209_224-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Inalcik1970209-224\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>209<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> To this end, Mehmed and his successor Bayezid, also encouraged and welcomed migration of the Jews from different parts of Europe, who were settled in Istanbul and other port cities like Salonica. In many places in Europe, Jews were suffering persecution at the hands of their Christian counterparts, such as in Spain, after the conclusion of the [Reconquista](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Reconquista/%22 "\\"Reconquista\\""). The tolerance displayed by the Turks was welcomed by the immigrants.\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mehmed_the_Conqueror_%281432_%E2%80%931481%29.jpg/250px-Mehmed_the_Conqueror_%281432_%E2%80%931481%29.jpg/%22)

A European bronze medal from the period of [Sultan Mehmed the Conqueror](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_II/%22 "\\"Mehmed"), 1481

\\n

The Ottoman economic mind was closely related to the basic concepts of state and society in the Middle East in which the ultimate goal of a state was consolidation and extension of the ruler's power, and the way to reach it was to get rich resources of revenues by making the productive classes prosperous.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Inalcik1970217_225-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Inalcik1970217-225\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>210<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The ultimate aim was to increase the state revenues without damaging the prosperity of subjects to prevent the emergence of social disorder and to keep the traditional organization of the society intact. The Ottoman economy greatly expanded during the early modern period, with particularly high growth rates during the first half of the eighteenth century. The empire's annual income quadrupled between 1523 and 1748, adjusted for inflation.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-226\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-226\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>211<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The organization of the treasury and chancery were developed under the Ottoman Empire more than any other Islamic government and, until the 17th century, they were the leading organization among all their contemporaries.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Black-2001_202-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Black-2001-202\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>187<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> This organisation developed a scribal bureaucracy (known as \\"men of the pen\\") as a distinct group, partly highly trained ulama, which developed into a professional body.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Black-2001_202-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Black-2001-202\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>187<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The effectiveness of this professional financial body stands behind the success of many great Ottoman statesmen.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-227\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-227\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>212<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ottoman_Banks_Archives_and_Research_Centre.jpg/250px-Ottoman_Banks_Archives_and_Research_Centre.jpg/%22)

The [Ottoman Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Bank/%22 "\\"Ottoman") was founded in 1856 in Constantinople. On 26 August 1896, the bank was [occupied](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Ottoman_Bank/%22 "\\"Occupation") by members of the [Armenian Revolutionary Federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation/%22 "\\"Armenian").

\\n

Modern Ottoman studies indicate that the change in relations between the Ottoman Turks and central Europe was caused by the opening of the new sea routes. It is possible to see the decline in the significance of the land routes to the East as Western Europe opened the ocean routes that bypassed the Middle East and the Mediterranean as parallel to the decline of the Ottoman Empire itself.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-228\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-228\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>213<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup class="\&quot;noprint" inline-template\"="" style="\&quot;white-space:nowrap;\&quot;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability/%22" title="\&quot;Wikipedia:Verifiability\&quot;"><span title="\&quot;The" material="" near="" this="" tag="" failed="" verification="" of="" its="" source="" citation(s).="" (september="" 2016)\"="">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> The [Anglo-Ottoman Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Anglo-Ottoman_Treaty/%22 "\\"Anglo-Ottoman"), also known as the [Treaty of Balta Liman](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Treaty_of_Balta_Liman/%22 "\\"Treaty") that opened the Ottoman markets directly to English and French competitors, can be seen as one of the staging posts along with this development.\\n

By developing commercial centers and routes, encouraging people to extend the area of cultivated land in the country and international trade through its dominions, the state performed basic economic functions in the Empire. But in all this, the financial and political interests of the state were dominant. Within the social and political system they were living in, Ottoman administrators could not see the desirability of the dynamics and principles of the capitalist and mercantile economies developing in Western Europe.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Inalcik1970218_229-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Inalcik1970218-229\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>214<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Economic historian [Paul Bairoch](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Paul_Bairoch/%22 "\\"Paul") argues that [free trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Free_trade/%22 "\\"Free") contributed to [deindustrialisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Deindustrialisation/%22 "\\"Deindustrialisation\\"") in the Ottoman Empire. In contrast to the [protectionism](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Protectionism/%22 "\\"Protectionism\\"") of China, Japan, and Spain, the Ottoman Empire had a [liberal trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Economic_liberalism/%22 "\\"Economic") policy, open to foreign imports. This has origins in [capitulations of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Capitulations_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Capitulations"), dating back to the first commercial treaties signed with France in 1536 and taken further with [capitulations](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Capitulation_\(treaty\)/%22 "\\"Capitulation") in 1673 and 1740, which lowered [duties](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Duty_\(economics\)/%22 "\\"Duty") to 3% for imports and exports. The liberal Ottoman policies were praised by British economists, such as [John Ramsay McCulloch](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/John_Ramsay_McCulloch/%22 "\\"John") in his *Dictionary of Commerce* (1834), but later criticized by British politicians such as Prime Minister Benjamin Disraeli, who cited the Ottoman Empire as \\"an instance of the injury done by unrestrained competition\\" in the 1846 [Corn Laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Corn_Laws/%22 "\\"Corn") debate.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-230\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-230\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>215<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

## Demographics

\\n

Main article: [Demographics of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Demographics")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ottoman_Smyrna.jpg/250px-Ottoman_Smyrna.jpg/%22)

[İzmir](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/%C4%B0zmir/%22 "\\"İzmir\\"") under Ottoman rule in 1900

\\n

A population estimate for the empire of 11,692,480 for the 1520–1535 period was obtained by counting the households in Ottoman tithe registers, and multiplying this number by 5.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Kabadayı_231-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Kabaday%C4%B1-231\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>216<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> For unclear reasons, the population in the 18th century was lower than that in the 16th century.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-232\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-232\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>217<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> An estimate of 7,230,660 for the first census held in 1831 is considered a serious undercount, as this census was meant only to register possible conscripts.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Kabadayı_231-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Kabaday%C4%B1-231\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>216<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Censuses of Ottoman territories only began in the early 19th century. Figures from 1831 onwards are available as official census results, but the censuses did not cover the whole population. For example, the 1831 census only counted men and did not cover the whole empire.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281_108-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281-108\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>94<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Kabadayı_231-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Kabaday%C4%B1-231\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>216<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> For earlier periods estimates of size and distribution of the population are based on observed demographic patterns.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-233\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-233\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>218<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Aerial_view_of_the_Galata_Bridge%2C_Istanbul_LCCN2003677084.jpg/250px-Aerial_view_of_the_Galata_Bridge%2C_Istanbul_LCCN2003677084.jpg/%22)

View of [Galata](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Galata/%22 "\\"Galata\\"") ([Karaköy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Karak%C3%B6y/%22 "\\"Karaköy\\"")) and the [Galata Bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Galata_Bridge/%22 "\\"Galata") on the [Golden Horn](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Golden_Horn/%22 "\\"Golden"), c. 1880–1893

\\n

However, it began to rise to reach 25–32 million by 1800, with around 10 million in the European provinces (primarily in the Balkans), 11 million in the Asiatic provinces, and around 3 million in the African provinces. Population densities were higher in the European provinces, double those in Anatolia, which in turn were triple the population densities of Iraq and [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Syria/%22 "\\"Syria\\"") and five times the population density of Arabia.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000110–111_234-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000110%E2%80%93111-234\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>219<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Towards the end of the empire's existence life expectancy was 49 years, compared to the mid-twenties in Serbia at the beginning of the 19th century.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000112_235-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000112-235\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>220<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Epidemic diseases and famine caused major disruption and demographic changes. In 1785 around one-sixth of the Egyptian population died from the plague and Aleppo saw its population reduced by twenty percent in the 18th century. Six famines hit Egypt alone between 1687 and 1731 and the last famine to hit Anatolia was four decades later.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000113_236-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000113-236\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>221<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The rise of port cities saw the clustering of populations caused by the development of steamships and railroads. Urbanization increased from 1700 to 1922, with towns and cities growing. Improvements in health and sanitation made them more attractive to live and work in. Port cities like Salonica, in Greece, saw its population rise from 55,000 in 1800 to 160,000 in 1912 and İzmir which had a population of 150,000 in 1800 grew to 300,000 by 1914.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000114_237-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000114-237\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>222<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-238\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-238\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>223<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Some regions conversely had population falls—Belgrade saw its population drop from 25,000 to 8,000 mainly due to political strife.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000114_237-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000114-237\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>222<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/20180107_Safranbolu_1945_%2839101010504%29.jpg/250px-20180107_Safranbolu_1945_%2839101010504%29.jpg/%22)

The town of [Safranbolu](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Safranbolu/%22 "\\"Safranbolu\\"") is one of the best preserved Ottoman villages.

\\n

Economic and political migrations made an impact across the empire. For example, the [Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Russian_Empire/%22 "\\"Russian") and Austria-Habsburg annexation of the Crimean and Balkan regions respectively saw large influxes of Muslim refugees—200,000 Crimean Tatars fleeing to Dobruja.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000115_239-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000115-239\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>224<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Between 1783 and 1913, approximately 5–7 million refugees arrived into the Ottoman Empire. Between the 1850s and World War I, about a million North Caucasian Muslims arrived in the Ottoman Empire as refugees.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamed-Troyansky202449_148-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamed-Troyansky202449-148\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>134<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Some migrations left indelible marks such as political tension between parts of the empire (e.g., Turkey and Bulgaria), whereas centrifugal effects were noticed in other territories, simpler demographics emerging from diverse populations. Economies were also impacted by the loss of artisans, merchants, manufacturers, and agriculturists.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000116_240-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuataertSpivey2000116-240\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>225<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Since the 19th century, a large proportion of Muslim peoples from the Balkans emigrated to present-day Turkey. These people are called *[Muhacir](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muhacir/%22 "\\"Muhacir\\"")*.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-241\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-241\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>226<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> By the time the Ottoman Empire came to an end in 1922, half of the urban population of Turkey was descended from Muslim refugees from Russia.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-books.google_b_140-5\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-books.google_b-140\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>126<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

### Language

\\n

Main article: [Languages of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Languages_of_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Languages")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg/250px-1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg/%22)

1911 Ottoman calendar shown in several different languages such as: Ottoman Turkish, Greek, Armenian, Hebrew, Bulgarian and French

\\n

[Ottoman Turkish](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish/%22 "\\"Ottoman") was the official language of the Empire.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-242\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-242\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>227<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> It was an [Oghuz](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Oghuz_languages/%22 "\\"Oghuz") [Turkic language](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkic_languages/%22 "\\"Turkic") highly influenced by [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Persian_language/%22 "\\"Persian") and [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Arabic/%22 "\\"Arabic\\""), though lower registries spoken by the common people had fewer influences from other languages compared to higher varieties used by upper classes and governmental authorities.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-243\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-243\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>228<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Turkish, in its Ottoman variation, was a language of military and administration since the nascent days of the Ottomans. The Ottoman constitution of 1876 did officially cement the official imperial status of Turkish.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-244\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-244\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>229<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The Ottomans had several influential languages: Turkish, spoken by the majority of the people in Anatolia and by the majority of Muslims of the Balkans except some regions such as [Albania](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Albania/%22 "\\"History"), [Bosnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Bosnia/%22 "\\"History")<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Bertold_Spuler_page_69_245-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Bertold_Spuler_page_69-245\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>230<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> and the [Megleno-Romanian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Megleno-Romanians/%22 "\\"Megleno-Romanians\\"")\-inhabited [Nânti](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/N%C3%A2nti/%22 "\\"Nânti\\"");<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-246\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-246\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>231<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Persian, only spoken by the educated;<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Bertold_Spuler_page_69_245-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Bertold_Spuler_page_69-245\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>230<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Arabic, spoken mainly in Egypt, the [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Levant/%22 "\\"Levant\\""), [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Arabia/%22 "\\"History"), Iraq, North Africa, [Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_Kuwait/%22 "\\"History") and parts of the [Horn of Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Horn_of_Africa/%22 "\\"Horn") and [Berber](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Berber_language/%22 "\\"Berber") in North Africa. In the last two centuries, usage of these became limited, though, and specific: Persian served mainly as a literary language for the educated,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Bertold_Spuler_page_69_245-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Bertold_Spuler_page_69-245\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>230<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> while [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Arabic/%22 "\\"Arabic\\"") was used for Islamic prayers. In the post-[Tanzimat](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tanzimat/%22 "\\"Tanzimat\\"") period French became the common Western language among the educated.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Strauss-2010_23-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Strauss-2010-23\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>17<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Because of a low literacy rate among the public (about 2–3% until the early 19th century and just about 15% at the end of the 19th century), ordinary people had to hire [scribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Scribe/%22 "\\"Scribe\\"") as \\"special request-writers\\" (*arzuhâlci*s) to be able to communicate with the government.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-247\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-247\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>232<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Some ethnic groups continued to speak within their families and neighborhoods ([mahalles](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mahalle/%22 "\\"Mahalle\\"")) with their own languages, though many non-Muslim minorities such as Greeks and Armenians only spoke Turkish.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavison196462_248-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavison196462-248\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>233<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In villages where two or more populations lived together, the inhabitants often spoke each other's language. In cosmopolitan cities, people often spoke their family languages; many of those who were not ethnic [Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkish_people/%22 "\\"Turkish") spoke Turkish as a second language.<sup class="\&quot;noprint" inline-template="" template-fact\"="" style="\&quot;white-space:nowrap;\&quot;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed/%22" title="\&quot;Wikipedia:Citation" needed\"=""><span title="\&quot;This" claim="" needs="" references="" to="" reliable="" sources.="" (july="" 2021)\"="">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\\n

\\n

### Religion

\\n

See also: [Millet (Ottoman Empire)](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\)/%22 "\\"Millet")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Portrait_Caliph_Abdulmecid_II.jpg/250px-Portrait_Caliph_Abdulmecid_II.jpg/%22)

[Abdülmecid II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abdulmejid_II/%22 "\\"Abdulmejid") was the last [caliph](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caliphate/%22 "\\"Caliphate\\"") of Islam and a member of the [Ottoman dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty/%22 "\\"Ottoman").

\\n

[Sunni Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sunni_Islam/%22 "\\"Sunni") was the prevailing *[Dīn](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Din_\(Arabic\)/%22 "\\"Din")* (customs, legal traditions, and religion) of the Ottoman Empire; the official *[Madh'hab](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Madhhab/%22 "\\"Madhhab\\"")* (school of Islamic [jurisprudence](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Jurisprudence/%22 "\\"Jurisprudence\\"")) was *[Hanafi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hanafi/%22 "\\"Hanafi\\"").*<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Gunduz_249-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Gunduz-249\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>234<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> From the early 16th century until the early 20th century, the Ottoman sultan also served as the [caliph](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caliphate/%22 "\\"Caliphate\\""), or politico-religious leader, of the [Muslim world](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muslim_world/%22 "\\"Muslim"). Most of the Ottoman Sultans adhered to [Sufism](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sufism/%22 "\\"Sufism\\"") and followed [Sufi orders](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sufi_orders/%22 "\\"Sufi"), and believed Sufism was the correct way to reach God.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-250\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-250\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>235<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Non-Muslims, particularly Christians and Jews, were present throughout the empire's history. The Ottoman imperial system was charactised by an intricate combination of official Muslim hegemony over non-Muslims and a wide degree of religious tolerance. While religious minorities were never equal under the law, they were granted recognition, protection, and limited freedoms under both Islamic and Ottoman tradition.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-emigrnonm_251-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-emigrnonm-251\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>236<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Until the second half of the 15th century, the majority of Ottoman subjects were Christian.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-4\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Benton-2001-207\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>192<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Non-Muslims remained a significant and economically influential minority, albeit declining significantly by the 19th century, due largely to migration and [secession](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Secession/%22 "\\"Secession\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-emigrnonm_251-1\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-emigrnonm-251\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>236<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The proportion of Muslims amounted to 60% in the 1820s, gradually increasing to 69% in the 1870s and 76% in the 1890s.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-emigrnonm_251-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-emigrnonm-251\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>236<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> By 1914, less than a fifth of the empire's population (19.1%) was non-Muslim, mostly made up of Jews and Christian Greeks, Assyrians, and Armenians.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-emigrnonm_251-3\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-emigrnonm-251\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>236<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

#### Islam

\\n

Main articles: [Islam in the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Islam_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Islam"), [Ottoman Caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate/%22 "\\"Ottoman"), and [Ottoman persecution of Alevis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_persecution_of_Alevis/%22 "\\"Ottoman")

\\n

See also: [Islam in Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Islam_in_Turkey/%22 "\\"Islam")

[Turkic peoples](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Turkic_peoples/%22 "\\"Turkic") practiced a form of [shamanism](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Shamanism/%22 "\\"Shamanism\\"") before adopting Islam. The [Muslim conquest of Transoxiana](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Transoxiana/%22 "\\"Muslim") under the [Abbasids](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate/%22 "\\"Abbasid") facilitated the spread of Islam into the Turkic heartland of Central Asia. Many Turkic tribes—including the [Oghuz Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Oghuz_Turks/%22 "\\"Oghuz"), who were the ancestors of both the Seljuks and the Ottomans—gradually converted to Islam and brought religion to Anatolia through their migrations beginning in the 11th century. From its founding, the Ottoman Empire officially supported the [Maturidi school of](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Maturidi/%22 "\\"Maturidi\\"") [Islamic theology](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Schools_of_Islamic_theology/%22 "\\"Schools"), which emphasized [human reason](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Reason/%22 "\\"Reason\\""), [rationality](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rationality/%22 "\\"Rationality\\""), the pursuit of science and [philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Islamic_philosophy/%22 "\\"Islamic") (*falsafa*).<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-252\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-252\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>237<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-253\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-253\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>238<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The Ottomans were among the earliest and most enthusiastic adopters of the [Hanafi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hanafi/%22 "\\"Hanafi\\"") school of Islamic jurisprudence,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-254\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-254\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>239<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> which was comparatively more flexible and discretionary in its rulings.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-255\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-255\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>240<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-256\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-256\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>241<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Istanbul_asv2021-10_img15_Y%C4%B1ld%C4%B1z_Hamidiye_Mosque.jpg/250px-Istanbul_asv2021-10_img15_Y%C4%B1ld%C4%B1z_Hamidiye_Mosque.jpg/%22)

The [Yıldız Hamidiye Mosque](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Y%C4%B1ld%C4%B1z_Hamidiye_Mosque/%22 "\\"Yıldız") in [Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Istanbul/%22 "\\"Istanbul\\""), Turkey

\\n

The Ottoman Empire had a wide variety of Islamic sects, including [Druze](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Druze/%22 "\\"Druze\\""), [Ismailis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Isma%27ilism/%22 "\\"Isma'ilism\\""), [Alevis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Alevism/%22 "\\"Alevism\\""), and [Alawites](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Alawites/%22 "\\"Alawites\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-257\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-257\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>242<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> [Sufism](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Sufism/%22 "\\"Sufism\\""), a diverse body of Islamic [mysticism](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mysticism/%22 "\\"Mysticism\\""), found fertile ground in Ottoman lands; many Sufi religious orders (*[tariqa](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Tariqa/%22 "\\"Tariqa\\"")*), such as the [Bektashi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Bektashi_Order/%22 "\\"Bektashi") and [Mevlevi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mevlevi_Order/%22 "\\"Mevlevi"), were either established, or saw significant growth, throughout the empire's history.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-258\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-258\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>243<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> However, some heterodox Muslim groups were viewed as heretical and even ranked below Jews and Christians in terms of legal protection; Druze were frequent targets of persecution,<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-259\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-259\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>244<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> with Ottoman authorities often citing the controversial rulings of [Ibn Taymiyya](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ibn_Taymiyyah/%22 "\\"Ibn"), a member of the conservative [Hanbali school](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hanbali/%22 "\\"Hanbali\\"").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-260\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-260\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>245<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In 1514, Sultan Selim I ordered the massacre of 40,000 Anatolian Alevis (*[Qizilbash](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Qizilbash/%22 "\\"Qizilbash\\"")*), whom he considered a [fifth column](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Fifth_column/%22 "\\"Fifth") for the rival [Safavid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Safavid_Iran/%22 "\\"Safavid").\\n

During Selim's reign, the Ottoman Empire saw an unprecedented and rapid expansion into the Middle East, particularly the [conquest of the entire Mamluk Sultanate of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Mamluk_War_\(1516%E2%80%931517\)/%22 "\\"Ottoman–Mamluk") on the early 16th century. These conquests further solidified the Ottoman claim of being an [Islamic caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Caliphate/%22 "\\"Caliphate\\""), although Ottoman sultans had been claiming the title of caliph since the reign of Murad I (1362–1389).<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Lambton-1995_25-2\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Lambton-1995-25\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>18<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The caliphate was officially transferred from the Mamluks to the Ottoman sultanate in 1517, whose members were recognized as caliphs until the [office's abolition on 3 March 1924](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Caliphate/%22 "\\"Abolition") by the [Republic of Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey/%22 "\\"Grand") (and the exile of the last caliph, [Abdülmecid II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Abdulmejid_II/%22 "\\"Abdulmejid"), to France).\\n

\\n

#### Christianity and Judaism

\\n

Main articles: [Christianity in the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Christianity") and [History of the Jews in the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"History")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Gennadios_II_and_Mehmed_II.jpg/250px-Gennadios_II_and_Mehmed_II.jpg/%22)

[Mehmed the Conqueror](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mehmed_II/%22 "\\"Mehmed") and Patriarch [Gennadius II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Gennadius_Scholarius/%22 "\\"Gennadius")

\\n

In accordance with the Muslim *[dhimmi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Dhimmi/%22 "\\"Dhimmi\\"")* system, the Ottoman Empire guaranteed limited freedoms to Christians, Jews, and other \\"[people of the book](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/People_of_the_Book/%22 "\\"People")\\", such as the right to worship, own property, and be exempt from the obligatory alms (*[zakat](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Zakat/%22 "\\"Zakat\\"")*) required of Muslims. However, non-Muslims (or *dhimmi*) were subject to various legal restrictions, including being forbidden to carry weapons, ride on horseback, or have their homes overlook those of Muslims; likewise, they were required to pay higher taxes than Muslim subjects, including the *[jizya](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Jizya/%22 "\\"Jizya\\""),* which was a key source of state revenue.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-261\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-261\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>246<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-262\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-262\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>247<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> Many Christians and Jews converted to Islam to secure full social and legal status, though most continued to practice their faith without restriction.\\n

The Ottomans developed a unique sociopolitical system known as the [millet](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\)/%22 "\\"Millet"), which granted non-Muslim communities a large degree of political, legal, and religious autonomy; in essence, members of a millet were subjects of the empire but not subject to the Muslim faith or Islamic law. A millet could govern its own affairs, such as raising taxes and resolving internal legal disputes, with little or no interference from Ottoman authorities, so long as its members were loyal to the sultan and adhered to the rules concerning *dhimmi.* A quintessential example is the ancient Orthodox community of [Mount Athos](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mount_Athos/%22 "\\"Mount"), which was permitted to retain its autonomy and was never subject to occupation or forced conversion; even special laws were enacted to protect it from outsiders.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-263\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-263\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>248<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

The [*Rum* Millet](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rum_Millet/%22 "\\"Rum"), which encompassed most Eastern Orthodox Christians, was governed by the Byzantine-era *[Corpus Juris Civilis](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Corpus_Juris_Civilis/%22 "\\"Corpus")* (Code of Justinian), with the [Ecumenical Patriarch](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople/%22 "\\"Ecumenical") designated the highest religious and political authority (*millet-bashi*, or [ethnarch](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ethnarch/%22 "\\"Ethnarch\\"")). Likewise, [Ottoman Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"History") came under the authority of the *[Haham Başı](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Hakham_Bashi/%22 "\\"Hakham"),* or Ottoman [Chief Rabbi](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Chief_Rabbi/%22 "\\"Chief"), while [Armenians](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenians/%22 "\\"Armenians\\"") were under the authority of the [chief bishop](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Catholicos_of_All_Armenians/%22 "\\"Catholicos") of the [Armenian Apostolic Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church/%22 "\\"Armenian").<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-Syed-2011_264-0\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-Syed-2011-264\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>249<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> As the largest group of non-Muslim subjects, the Rum Millet enjoyed several special privileges in politics and commerce; however, Jews and Armenians were also well represented among the wealthy merchant class, as well as in public administration.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-265\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-265\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>250<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-266\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-266\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>251<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

Some modern scholars consider the millet system to be an early example of [religious pluralism](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Religious_pluralism/%22 "\\"Religious"), as it accorded minority religious groups official recognition and tolerance.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-267\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-267\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>252<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n

### Social-political-religious structure

\\n

See also: [Rayah](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Rayah/%22 "\\"Rayah\\"")

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Subject_Nationalities_of_the_German_Alliance_%281917%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Subject_Nationalities_of_the_German_Alliance_%281917%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/%22)

Ethnic map of the Ottoman Empire in 1917. Black = Bulgars and Turks, Red = Greeks, Light yellow = Armenians, Blue = Kurds, Orange = Lazes, Dark Yellow = Arabs, Green = Nestorians

\\n

Beginning in the early 19th century, society, government, and religion were interrelated in a complex, overlapping way that was deemed inefficient by Atatürk, who systematically dismantled it after 1922.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-268\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-268\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>253<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-269\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-269\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>254<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> In Constantinople, the Sultan ruled two distinct domains: the secular government and the religious hierarchy. Religious officials formed the Ulama, who had control of religious teachings and theology, and also the Empire's judicial system, giving them a major voice in day-to-day affairs in communities across the Empire (but not including the non-Muslim millets). They were powerful enough to reject the military reforms proposed by Sultan [Selim III](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Selim_III/%22 "\\"Selim"). His successor Sultan [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Mahmud_II/%22 "\\"Mahmud") (r. 1808–1839) first won ulama approval before proposing similar reforms.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-270\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-270\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>255<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The secularisation program brought by Atatürk ended the ulema and their institutions. The caliphate was abolished, madrasas were closed down, and the sharia courts were abolished. He replaced the Arabic alphabet with Latin letters, ended the religious school system, and gave women some political rights. Many rural traditionalists never accepted this secularisation, and by the 1990s they were reasserting a demand for a larger role for Islam.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-271\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-271\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>256<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup>\\n

\\n![](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Istanbul_asv2021-11_img71_StAnthony_of_Padua_Church.jpg/250px-Istanbul_asv2021-11_img71_StAnthony_of_Padua_Church.jpg/%22)

The original [Church of St. Anthony of Padua, Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Church_of_St._Anthony_of_Padua,_Istanbul/%22 "\\"Church") was built in 1725 by the local Italian community of Istanbul.

\\n

The Janissaries were a highly formidable military unit in the early years, but as Western Europe modernized its military organization technology, the Janissaries became a reactionary force that resisted all change. Steadily the Ottoman military power became outdated, but when the Janissaries felt their privileges were being threatened, or outsiders wanted to modernize them, or they might be superseded by the cavalrymen, they rose in rebellion. The rebellions were highly violent on both sides, but by the time the Janissaries were suppressed, it was far too late for Ottoman military power to catch up with the West.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-272\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-272\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>257<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup><sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-273\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-273\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>258<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> The political system was transformed by the destruction of the [Janissaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Janissary/%22 "\\"Janissary\\""), a powerful military/governmental/police force, which revolted in the [Auspicious Incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Auspicious_Incident/%22 "\\"Auspicious") of 1826. Sultan Mahmud II crushed the revolt, executed the leaders and disbanded the large organization. That set the stage for a slow process of modernization of government functions, as the government sought, with mixed success, to adopt the main elements of Western bureaucracy and military technology.\\n

The Janissaries had been recruited from Christians and other minorities; their abolition enabled the emergence of a Turkish elite to control the Ottoman Empire. A large number of ethnic and religious minorities were tolerated in their own separate segregated domains called millets.<sup id="\&quot;cite_ref-274\&quot;" class="\&quot;reference\&quot;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/%22#cite_note-274\%22"><span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">[</span>259<span class="\&quot;cite-bracket\&quot;">]</span></a></sup> They were primarily [Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Ottoman_Greeks/%22 "\\"Ottoman"), [Armenian](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/Armenians_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"Armenians"), or [Jewish](https://en.wikipedia.org/%22/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Ottoman_Empire/%22 "\\"History").
